Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	They would call the old "wound healer," and you should apply to the affected area that has this disease with or without hair, then make three cuts evenly along the length of the front; and one of the cuts as close as possible to the top of the front, and the other two at the ribs above the papers, and guard against incising the arteries that are at the ribs above the papers; and move your hand away from the continuation of the two jaws, and for each wound, a quantity of three drops through the joins; and have prepared a piece of sponge and much cloth to soak up the blood, then boil the medicine from this form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	From the incision that is made from the temple to the second incision; and scrape all that is between the two cuts to the entire syphilitic sore which is above the bone, then make another incision from the other side of the same second incision, and then extract this sponge.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If you push the tool that is called "cultellaire" into the first cut, and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side is soft, not very sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the sharp edge of the tool towards the back of the cut, and the soft edge towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the other cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And to all the vessels that descend from the head as far as the eyes until the incision is continued just enough to open the wound, and then make another incision in the same place on the other side; then extract the blood equally, and express the wound for the blood taken; then put a tent of old cotton in each incision, and put moistened cloths of wine and oil and vinegar over them, and guard that abscesses do not come; and the next day remove the leather, and apply great amounts of fresh turpentine, then the cure of basilicon with rose oil, and other cures that are used to heal wounds, until they are healed.
dou reume des eulz	For the eyes' pricking at their base
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When anyone comes for cauterization as usual, and you see the eyes tightly closed and small, and weakened vision, and burnt papers; and the hairs are shaved, and where the shaving is done, it causes great pain, and the limbs are numb; therefore, these accidents and that cauterization come only from many wounds, and the healing process that is, if this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to turn his head back, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another wide at the top of the nose.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	Starting from the right temple wound to the left, and make the incision up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the temples that move at the jaw; and when the bone is exposed, suck all the blood onto a sponge, then clean between the two lips of the wound and put cotton wool, and linen; then bandage with moistened cloths in wine and oil, and guard against abscess formation; when it is removed, it is necessary to rub the bone until charcoal begins to form, then care for things that cause char, which are done by injecting char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	Take two parts of wheat flour and four parts of brimstone, and make a poultice; and administer it in these wounds to draw out char throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the blocking of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that which enters the ears is one of the four things: grains, wax, stone or similar thing like iron; or seeds, such as beans, peas, or similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it enters the ear in the form of stone or other thing that does not stick to the ear, it does not grow in the ear, so put the ear to the sunlight.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, if you drop a little purple oil or mustard oil, then facilitate extraction; and it causes nausea, and the nose stops when the sneezing comes, and put around the ear pieces of cloth or wool; and keep the ear up.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Often heals by this treatment; and if it does not heal, then apply gentle extraction with small pins, of which the form is as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it heals with the pins, it is good; if not, then apply gentle extraction with small needles; and if it does not heal by this method, make a hole in the ear drum very hard so that nothing can enter with the needle; then remove it properly, for often it heals as we have said; and if it does not heal in this way, take some gauze and place it over the ear, and put any instrument that is sharp on it, and put a little cotton around; then press the gauze on the drum or whatever else, and remove it.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not jump from all these things that we have said, you must quickly cut the ear to prevent abscess and swelling; and the way of the cut is that you first clean the pain of the cephalic, and extract the pus according to the measure of its virtue, then place the pain between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small cut at the root of the ear at the grease or where it depends; and let the cut be as a moon, until you reach the bone, then remove it according to your power, and suck vigorously at your mouth; and the cure until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is small grains that are in and it swells, administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, administer the following remedy subtly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and administer an incision of that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make it too thin when you think the grains are moist due to earwax, until you have made many pieces; then extract with fine forceps and succiner, as we have said, so that the extraction is aligned.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the case of the ear, then when it is sharp it is necessary that the hairs use sneezing of condition firsts, and widen the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let it lie across the ear itself or the sharp part.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps out due to heaven, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If not from heaven, take many small and light stones according to the length of your finger, and heat them in the fire; and put the hairs one or two through the ear, and strike upwards from the other foot, and with another stone on top of the stone that is in the ear; and do not stop hitting with stone after stone until all the sharp part is out, and thus the whole thing comes out; and if you see, take a rod, and put one of the hairs into the ear, and the other hair grip with fire until the thinnest rod is burned; then do the same with other rods until all the sharp part is out, as we have said in the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the animal, if it is of small size, like a mouse and similar things, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, where one can feel it, then alleviate extraction with pincers; and it is the lightest thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the division and if you cannot cure it, then look into the ear with the sunlight: if there are no worms, then remove them with fine pincers, and if not, then take the cotton of which this is made.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And be narrow below and wide above.

And if it is made of silver or lead, pierce the small pores and pour over the surface to distill; and to press during the distillation, use a well-made instrument of lead for this purpose, and if you see that the tool becomes dull, take the razor and wrap it around the tip evenly with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicine you see in the bowl, and the bowl should be in the ear; then blow through the razor all the cotton, and press your hand temperately until the oil is distilled or the smell from the ear; and the bad smell is inside, and the distillation should be slightly warm, just as it is distilled in the ear; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the stiffness of the ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without some stiffness in their ears; and the same thing happens to men by stiffness of wound, or from a splinter inside the ear, and this stiffness never comes out from in front of the ear, if one cannot see it; and it always comes out from behind the ear, and one sees it well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, that which comes out from in front, if one cannot see it, is from great pain in many positions, and in this case, where one sees, one must put the ear with the wrong side up to the sun; and look inside: if you see the opening of the eardrum at the same time as this space:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let the smoke and steam go in front and behind all around, so that it does not blow into the ear; if the opilation is of horn or leather of the ear, then hold it with fine pincers, and the copper lightly, until that horn is completely burned.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the opilation is in the ear, then take a fine knife lightly and heat it a little in the fire, then put it on the copper where the ear is.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the opilation that the pain feels gritty to hear, lightly pierce, and make sure you do not injure the nerves of the ear; then put in the ear a tent according to the width of the wound, and moisten it with Egyptian egg.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not move the wound until it is healed, or take a tent and moisten it with high rosewater, and powder vitriol on top; and if you see swelling in the ear, it is recommended that you remove the tent and apply another tent moistened with rosewater and wax, as long as the swelling is removed; then cure it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if blood comes out, soak an sponge and wipe with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that remove the outflow of blood which are used to treat distillations.
de la char des papieres	of the paper of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the method for treating the eyes when they are wet and dry: extend them with forceps and pincers, and remove the root of their eyelashes; then apply a piece of glass broken into pieces to the eye.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if there is no decortication, then cauterize the lens with a fine cautery, and the cauterizer after incision is useful; and many times they recur, but nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the gravel
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Often in papers come things that seem to be gravel in their form and hardness, and because of this disease is called "hail," and it is a mixture of large moisture above and below; the work is such: if the hail moves from one side to another, it is an easy thing to know; then make it wide, then scrape lightly each part, then take pincers and remove it.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you do not cover it with a puncture in the paper, it does not hurt the patient; and if the fracture is large, it gathers at a seam, and cure as long as it is healthy; and if it is small, do not make force, for the wounds restore quickly and heal.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the splinter is descending into the inner part of the ear towards the upper part, turn the paper, and place the splinter on a pair of tweezers, and hold it with forceps and press from one side and the other; and if the paper is displaced by incision, it does not matter; and when the splinter is removed, pour in some strong salt water, and cure the wound until the hairs are healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is smeared on paper above the eyes, and it has more effect in children than in adults, and it hurts their eyes, and they vomit it in the morning, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears flow to their eyes; and because they sleep on their faces, they have their papers wet beneath them that swell and appear covered with exinach which appears in the oil.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press on the shoulder to your touch and feel the joint move between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the way of the work is such that the hairs put their head in your hand; and then take a cloth of linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the joint on each part, then place it over it; and press on one side and the other, so that the joint is assembled within the circle; then make a small cut at the edge of the skin, not larger than the wound made on the vein; and cut the skin until you come to the joint; and in many positions of the joint, according to the form of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Extract the towel from all around you between your hands, and turn your hand to the right and left as far as it can spread; and beware that you do not insert it into the wound, that you do not bring the whole of the material close to the skin, that you do not wound it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if it does not exit at the beginning of the wound, then lightly scrape the wound until it opens; then extract it as we have said, then clean the towels in hot and cold water, and put on the limb, and bandage it well.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who break and put on the cloth to corrupt the moisture that remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the healer as long as they are healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient comes to the healer with an abscess that is not ready, then the healer should apply dressings moistening until they are healthy.
des poilz des papieres	of hairs of papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai. It is necessary to place the head of the badly aligned joint in your hand, then turn the paper with oil to your right hand; if it is converted, it is good; if not, if there is a needle at the end of the thread above; and if it is on the other side of the margin of the paper where the hairs grow between these hairs, and draw the thread above the paper, and return the razor; then in the part outside the paper, outside the hair, covering all the skin from the great calf to the small; then pull the thread, and place outside the paper a small cotton and bandage, then above the paper a figure of a sling, like the belly of a mart, and thus it is necessary that the figure be according to the amount that you saw lift the paper which is divided into all.

puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then apply this remedy evenly according to the form that is here:

If you cannot hold the needles, and the thing is not even, take a needle or it has a thread, and the thread into the shape; and the other thread over the great arm, and the second thread over the small one, and assemble between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin where you have signed, as we have told you, then assemble the two lips of the wound by sewing, and cure it until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, soothe it with salve and similar soothing ointments; and never once has the hair of the paper been converted: so you must use what we have said about the incision; but the sewing on one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of wounds is as follows: first, convert the paper and the needle according to what I have said, and then make two needles by art, and two threads subtly as long as the paper and its width; and connect the two ends of the two threads where you hold the threads; then assemble them subtly above the paper of the oil, and strain the two needles from the two parts to form a whole; and leave it thus for some time, and the skin that was stretched will die and decay and rot, until it falls off by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it takes too long, if the connection is strong, then cure it until it is healed; and when the wound has been dressed, and if the paper has been removed, and the hairs will not grow back; and this is the form of the two needles that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of length and width.
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a thin needle, and you thread silk thread so fine; then assemble the hairs and hold both subtly, and let the lengths of the threads be a palm long; then order the other thin silk thread briefly in the hunt, and hold the heads of the hairs together, and place it on your hand; and let it be outside the sun so that the work is not discolored, for this is a subtle and fine work, then pierce the needle throughout the hunt in the root of the hair raised, and make it perforate the paper gently until you remove it from the natural hair; then stretch the hair up to the hunt, and pierce that hair, if there are one, two, three or more; then stretch your hand until the hairs come out throughout the hunt with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the bone is treated and the hairs do not come with it, then you must reset the bone to its original position, following the same path as before, until the bone is fully healed and you can see it through oil; then, if necessary, reset the bone and apply oil, and close it and leave it for two or three days, until the hairs grow back in their place and the char is formed on top; and if the hairs are small, accompany one long hair from the lambs' wool, and raise it with the other where you leave it, until it is fully extended and then lift it.
de la porriture de l’oil	of the oil of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the palsy, comes in the oil, there are two ways: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it comes by sudden injury, or cutting, or cauterization, and similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the method of treatment in this is that you break that suture, and dry the lips of it, and put within tents of linen, and bind it until it is healed; and you should only use in its care things that dry and constrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but in the work of things that are softening, such as fenugreek; and the rose of vinegar or altee and seeds of linseed oil should be cooked, and an ointment made from it, and wrap a tent around it, and care for this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your care are that you take precautions that it does not sound as it was before; and this work that we have said is only to guide it so that it does not return as it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the oil that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease that is dislocated which truly is called "axacrati", and is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wound and cutting and cauterizing and similar things; and the way of the work in this is that you grasp a needle, in which it has a double thread, and the thread in the oil, and make it pierce from the left calf to the right, so that the thread comes out in two pieces of the oil; then the oil is placed on top of the needle, and the cloth is spread wide.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper's shape returns according to what it should be, it is good; if not, take the razor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two cuts where the edges of the incision you have made meet; and let the corners of the two cuts be sharp so that when they are joined together, the shape will be as if it were a letter with a straight edge; then remove that char, according to the quantity that its cost is from the paper, then add the two missing parts, and sew them with a thread of linen; then care for what we have said about mollifying medicines and tents, until they are healed.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a cut or stitch or cauterization, it is necessary that you make a plain cut outside of the hairs and papers, as I have said before; then squeeze between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and one must do the work according to the form of the disease, for it is very different in form, and the wise masters apply all possible means to how they can make the figure return to its natural form; and the patients themselves, according to what is necessary for work and instruments in many positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	The paper is soaked.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this suturing is done by unskilled people in a somewhat way that the paper above is glued with the white of the oil, and it cannot move or do its natural workings, then you must therefore go to the outside of the paper with the point of a razor, and lift it up; and extend it with pincers, until you scrape off what is hard under the subtle skin, which should not be too hard nor too thin, so that the hairs cannot suffer that the skin is too hard and does not burn the oil; and let your incision, from which you scrape this assembly, cleanly, so that the paper regains its natural form; and is whole that entire assembly, and never use in acidic salty oil, and lift with alkaline sweet water, and with colloid; then put between the paper and the oil a linen cloth, and put above the oil wool moistened in abund of honey; and after the wound heals use colloid and other healing things until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the elbow joint
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways the elbow joint can be affected: one is nervous and resembles a hard, rough surface, and the other is not nervous but resembles a frozen white moisture, which when touched with iron and heated with pincers cannot be removed; and both start near the large arm and grow slowly until they cover the entire eyeball and light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of incision is that the evil spirits put their head in your hand, then work the eyes; and lift the paper to your hand, then bend the elbow with pincers of small doubled-up, and place it above; then take a needle, and put some horsehair, or sheep hair, or cow hair, and strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and insert it into the elbow, and push the needle through the entire needle, and tie the elbow with a thread and place it above, and scrape all the hair on the side of the elbow that shows the bone and the silk to the hair just above, then cover the remaining in the root of the arm to all the subtle sinew and with small forces, and leave the natural skin of the arm, so that by the incision the usual tears do not come out; and once it has been extended only to the elbow, and the thread, as we have said; then scrape on all the soft sinew of which this is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful that the spatula does not touch the charred flesh and break it, and that the prunel does not pierce; and after the incision pour a little bit of broken silk oil, and a poultice made of litharge, and leave it on the other side; then care for the wound until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the joint is not yet nervous, and you cannot insert the needle, and the pins cannot enter, often this resemblance of a joint of medicines is cured; and they are born as I have said in the division, and if you see them covered, then work the oil of the evil, and take the spatula lightly with a slightly sharp edge according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And gently rub the angle above subtly, and if you see that it does not ease and the reason is close, then sprinkle from your mouth into the oil collar made of litharge and red oil and silk broth, and extinguish the oil just after; then continue the other work according to this same method, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary to you in the oil, as an abscess, then milk, and first cure the abscess until it is healed, then continue the work as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh on the arm is black and night-like due to great harm, then soak it in oil at night, and cover a part of it and not all at once, until tears come out; then pour red wine colloquy which is made of litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows above the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men never grow red flesh, and cover the pupil and hold it above the papers and turn it to the end, and it seems like a baluster rose; and the work is that the hairs put their head in your healthy skin, then work the eyelids, and cut all that flesh with suitable incisions for this, and support it with force; then cover the first flesh, and go all scraping to the razor just to the end, and be careful not to bleach the oil at the work; and let the incision of the spatula that we have said in the incision of the finger and as small forces of which we take the base, as the form after this chapter demonstrates; and when the incision is accomplished and all the flesh is removed, then use the oil of silk broken or you distill red wine colloquy and similar corrosive medicines, and put on the oil above cotton with a bit of wool, so that it is ensured to prevent abscess; and if nothing remains, and the skin does not cover, and you doubt abscess, then leave the oil and cure the abscess with things calming abscess; then return to your work until it is healthy, and thus make many flesh is treated in oil by this way.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you apply the cure of each weakness of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in iron work; and do not put your hand in any of these works until you see that this member is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the eyes'
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Red veins that are covered over the eye, and take away from the sight their work and weaken the eye always.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The work is therefore to the first that you look at whether this eye, in which there is redness, is better, and if there is no other disease besides the redness; then the work in this way: command the pain to put its head in your healthy eye, then suspend those veins all around according to its wisdom, and let the circles be subtle double in this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let them be done twice a day, once in the morning and once in the evening, in this manner:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then gently rub those veins subtly, and suck out the blood after an hour, until you can remove those veins from the oil; and be careful not to prick the oil with the points of the spatulas, and do this work at noon in front of the sun, and be very fervent in your work so that you do not cause any harm to those veins; and when you have done this, distill green and red willow charcoal into the oil to corrupt what remains from before.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you cannot gather all the herbs in that hour, then apply a plaster over the oil of things that calm the pain of the eyes, and let it remain for some time until the pain is relieved and the risk of abscess is ensured, then resume according to this method as long as it is not healed; and this is the form of forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	from the hole of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The mire, if often called "arissati", is cured by cauterization and medicine, as I have said before, and it is not healed, then you should engage in what you did to the abscess, where it must die, and remove all the moisture that is there, until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed, and you see corruption and blackness, then the instrument of that which is in this form; it is called "rough chisel", and it should be made of iron from the same chisel, and it should be pointed as a lime if it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	Then place the rough chisel on the end of the bone, then turn it between your two fingers, and press your hand a little until you feel that that corruption is removed; and do this once, then restore the bone to remedies to dry it out.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the bone is still sound, and the wound is healed, and the body of the bone is sound, and remains thus for forty days, and it does not reopen and is not infected, and no bad accident happens, then it is considered healthy; if not, there is no other method than to bring the fistula back to the opening of the sinus according to this form: and you should uncover the bone the second time with iron, and by wet medicines, and when it is exposed again take the foret according to this form, and make the head of the nail at three angles, and make the tail of the nail attenuated as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place it above the bone of the arm, and move your hand away from the oil and the flesh, then return to the whole forearm until it pierces the bone and the patient feels the pain as if it comes from inside if he holds his hand on his neck; and when the medicine is dried, as I have indicated, and when the char begins to harden and stiffen the muscles, then the matter goes to the neck; so it is a lighter thing for the pain.
de l’issue de l’oil	from the end of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes are widely open and do not move to the neck, nor are they affected, then you must tie the pain; then clean it, then put on leeches or a hot iron to draw out blood, then put on the oil mixed with acacia, aloe, incense, and sarcocollis, and then strain the oil, and apply the plaster with bandages and cloths; the manner of the cloths is that you take cloths that are soft enough, and double each one in four, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity that the eyes need; then strain it through a hard bendeil form, and start the leeches again to draw out blood without hurting; then remove the leeches and leave the oil strained day and night, and if the oil does not improve, then you must strain it more; then remove the mixture after the day and night, and if you see the oil improving, it is good; if not, then start the plaster and cloths and the mixture and leeches again until they are healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	forced removal of torn cloth
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions occur in the torn cloth, then open it, and if it is thick like a grain of resin, and is easily seen; then if you see that it covers, the work is such that you should put a needle into the root of the part below this above, then put another needle or it has double the thickness of the part of the arm; and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the thread double and tie a part of the cloth around, and hold it well, then remove the needle and put the salve on the wound with enough oil; and let it stay until the thread cuts with the cloth, then care for the oil of things comforting until the wound is healed; and once the wound is covered by a piece of cloth, tant qu’elle soit sanee.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes appear greatly protruded, prick them with a fine needle that comes from the front of the oil, and draw out the moisture and wipe off the eyelids, and place them together immediately; then remove them as much as they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the front of the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease that is called "alcunnati" is nothing but a collection of oil that descends in the oil, resembling an acute descending, and it is not sharp; and the way of appearance of the work is such that you make the evil sit above the seat, well-dressed and straight, then take the head between your hands from two parts, and move the mover until you see the collection coming to the top to your eyes; then let it be hidden, and do not wipe off and do not disperse the light, and see the evil things as they should be; and if it does not descend, it is not well-dressed as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the painful part is placed between your hands, then take the thin spatula and make it slide over the corneal suture and the cornea and the crown, as long as the wound is open; and when it is open, then pour in hot acidic oil mixed with honey, or acidic or fenugreek is boiled and mixed with honey, then cure it with other treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the acidic oils
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have experienced similar cases in the division, and what is necessary to pierce; if it works according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary for you to place the painful joint between your crossed hands, outside of the light for the sun, and with clean oil pressed firmly; then place the paper of oil in your right hand if the joint is on the left side, or in your left hand if the joint is on the right side; then take in your right hand if the joint is on the left side, or in your left hand if the joint is on the right side, the instrument called «almagda», or in your right hand if the joint is on the right side; then place the point of the «almagda» instrument above the crown of the oil in the thinnest part of the elbow, then press the «almagda» instrument virtuously, and hold your hand until it pierces through the oil, and feels that «almagda» comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way «almagda» be at the beginning of the space from the golden needle to the end of the noir; and this is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper for the clarity of the cloth, and then place the instrument above it or at the sharp edge, then express it one after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if he has sharp eyesight now, he will see the hairs in front of him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting a little, and if he has sharp eyesight again, put the cautery with the instrument, and when it is stuck and does not go up, gently rotate your hand back and forth; then put a small piece of cloth over the eye and leave it inside.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put in the eye that is soaked or otherwise wet with rose oil and plenty of honey, and bandage it with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those who are of our time, put on top with plenty of honey.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the sharp object cannot enter the oil due to its hardness, because there are some men who have very hard eyes, then you must use the tool called "alberit", which has the following form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Therefore, pierce only the conjunctive, and do not move too much in front, but make the eye subtle, then push the hard object, as we have said; and at the completion of the work compare to the pain and sleep that occurs, in which he sleeps on his back in the dark room; and avoid all movements, take light meals, and do not move his head to the right or left, and tie according to his disposition until tomorrow; then release him in this same dark room, and test his vision, and show him some things, and then return the bandage by the next day; and you should not do this in the first hour of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you raise the eyelid, because the sharp object hurts quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When abscesses come, you should apply warm oil before the seventh hour, and strengthen it with what satisfies the abscess; and when it is calmed, then remove the bandage and put on a new one to cover any opening, and let it be set in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then slowly bring it out of the house little by little, and let it return to its place; and do not let any disciple intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Sometimes we were in Yrach, who told us that in some countries people would pierce the acupuncture point, because of which the aigue would succeed, but I have never seen any in our land, nor have I read any in the books of the ancients; perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the similarities of the shapes of almonds, because those who do not know them see them as such; and they are made of pure tin properly.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And their heads are of the same subtlety as their tails, and the back in three angles bent.
de la char sor le neis	of the horn for the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never are born or grow noses of different horns, for which there are some that seem like scorpions at the mouth of the feet; and if there are such, or if there is a horn with a bad color, and if there is a soft horn of good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case, of those horns which are soft and not enchanted, it is necessary that you make the pain between your hands against the sun; and work their noses, and pour the one in those horns, and remove them; for this is how you can hold the subtle sharpness of a part, until you know that that horn is all softened.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains anything that cannot be removed with any instrument, open it all the way to the deepest tools subtly and lightly, so that nothing remains; and if it is a pus-filled abscess, wipe it clean as it should be; and if it is malignant abscesses, hurry and cauterize it until the wound is no longer wet and all the charred flesh is removed, then pour out or drain off the pus and the sharp and sour wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it does not drain properly, and moisture enters the palate, then remove it as soon as possible; and if it does not pierce as it should, then there is charred flesh in the bone above, which prevents the instruments from cutting: therefore, you must first insert a thin needle into the patient's mouth, and pull out the bad parts with equal space between each one; and put the bad parts of the thread into the patient's mouth through the opening of the neck, and draw it out until it comes out through the mouth; and many times they do this in schools, and it is an easy task for those who want to do it; then hold the part that comes out of the neck with one hand, and the other part that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and cut them one after the other as we do.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this until you know that the newborn has not corrupted that stool, then remove the filth, soak the blood, and clean the filament in an Egyptian method, and return it to the nose as before; do this three times or more, until the filaments corrode all that remains of the stool; and then put or place a plug in the nose for several days until it is healed, and if it has a need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, by which one distills oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And it should be of silver or bronze, shaped like an open lamp, such as a plug, and use it in the same way; and if you see, make a closed plug, and let the instruments be plain for purging the head; and have one hand on the head to hold when heating the oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the worm on the nose
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Often a disease arises at the tip of the nose called "telul", which grows and becomes large over time; and for this reason, it is necessary to cover it from the beginning, and to remove all of it, then place the cauterizing fire or medicine on the affected area; and if one delays in covering it when it is large, if it is hard, of poor color, and insensitive: if one does not touch it with iron because it is an infected abscess, for when one covers it once, great harm comes to the patient; and if the abscess is softly touched, not of poor color, and you see that one can cover it all, then remove the infection and cover the affected area without fear, and cure the patient of similar and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the bone is cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	If any solution of continuity comes from one of these cartilages, it is of little use, as in no men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, it is best to check if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then bring together the two lips at a seam, then treat it until it is healed; and if the lips are already decayed from one side and the other, it is necessary to scorch all the parts of their edge until they heal, then bring together the two lips at a seam, and hold them, and powder with powder of blood from a dragon, and frankincense; and put on the powders a piece of strong or other plaster, and leave it until it eats through it, then treat the wound until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way of sewing is such that you assemble the stitches: either with needles, as we have said in the sewing of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	Some people have abscesses within the lips, hard and small like grains, and smaller and larger ones; therefore, it is necessary to turn the lips, and prick each one, and take them with pincers and scrape each part; then fill the cavity after incision with broken glass powder, until the wound is not dampened; and then apply a poultice of dry things until the wound is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the toothache
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the toothache arises from the gums due to decay, which the ancients called "albulus"; therefore, it is necessary to support it with forceps, and cover its root, and let out the pus or blood; then put on the tooth with a broken piece of glass, or other powders that strengthen and dry; and if the toothache returns after the incision, and often does, then cover it again, and cauterize: if it does not return after the cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments for covering.
des sordens	of deafness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes the teeth are gathered at the tip of the gums, between the gums and the teeth, sharp and painful scars; and sometimes they are black and yellow and green, until the corruption reaches the gum, and are foul-smelling teeth; so you should put the pain between your hands, and its name should be in your holy book, and grind the teeth or the scars that appear, until there is nothing left; and thus make the black and green, and yellow and other stains, until they are clean; and if you remove what is at the first layer, it is good; if not, start again on the second day and the third, until you have removed everything; and be aware that the teeth have different forms of tools to grind, according to what the work demonstrates, because the file that is used to grind between the teeth has other shapes than those that are used to grind the teeth. And these shapes and others should be prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating the toothache that you delay pulling it as long as possible, for no one should do this; for it is a substance very high and therefore we have no excuse to pull it out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then when the toothache is too painful to bear, you must be certain that the tooth is dead.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain of the toothache is relieved, and you should check if it is a holy tooth, and pull out the good tooth; and afterwards, the pain does not leave until the evil is extracted, for we have already done this to these saints; and when you are sure that the dead tooth is dead, you must burn around the tooth at all points; then pull it out with your fingers or fine forceps at first and then, as long as it is well loosened, then firmly fix the forceps; and let the one who has the toothache in your saint between your teeth, and hold it well so that it does not move.
