Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After straightening the tooth correctly without breaking, and if it does not spring back, take one of these instruments and gently press it into each part lightly, and shake it as you did first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the tooth is pierced and crushed, it is necessary to fill it with rags where the cavities are; and if the instrument subtly has hooks, so that it does not break when pulling; and it is very important to work around the gum to ease the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful not to break it, and that a part remains, and reapply the pain by the greater pain of the root of the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be aware that you do not act in such a way as the ignorant ones who, by their haste and their boldness, break the chariot once and for all, and do not bring back what we have told; but they bring about great disease from the roots that they leave behind, or from the chariot that they break, as we often see; and when the denser part is removed, wash the limb with wine or vinegar and salt; and if blood comes out again, which often happens, use the leg in a solution of boiled oil; and if it does not work, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, by which one moves the first tooth, should be long pointed and large-handed, so they do not bend when you pull out the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be large-bodied so they do not bend when pulling, and they should be made of well-forged iron, and they should have teeth to hold.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when pulling, then you should put a soft cotton cloth on the wound or 2 or 3.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the wound is softened, then insert the forceps called "algefri," by which the patient resembles a beak of care; and they should be made like a shell, and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these needles, then it is necessary that you cut around the root completely, and put the instrument called «althali», which is a spoon, of which this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And if it is too thick so that it does not break in two, and if the root jumps out through the hole, it is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the shapes come hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use this instrument that has two prongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in the region of the teeth, and of this instrument which looks like large needles, of which this is the shape:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And this instrument, except that it cannot break, and sharp enough to cut through many dense materials; and also other tools, which I will not mention; and the wise masters find their own tool by themselves, according to what their observations and the disease show them, because there are some diseases where the ancients did not teach about the tool due to the diversity of use; and if they break the cart or other bones, or it does not work, if they look for tools that they should have, as I have told you, and help with gestures, from which this form is:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let the bones be large and well-holding to hold the bone, so it does not escape, but it can hold and remove; then restore the limb with appropriate medicines according to this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if the doctor has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural course, and its shape is ugly, and especially in young women, it is necessary that you cut out the tooth if it is not in the right place, and it cannot be straightened or filed: then use this instrument which has a shape like a small beak, and is made of iron with sharp edges:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the copper poker gently and slowly moves over the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be removed, then the copper poker removes it as follows:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	It is also like the poker of which one makes the arrows; and in pokering the tooth gently and slowly moves over it for a little while, so that it does not move until it breaks; then at the end with any sharp instrument, and if the tooth is too thin and it bleeds the tongue, then one must remove the roughness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	when they are toothache
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front is aching, whether by pressure or by falling, and the pain cannot be relieved because it does not stop moving, and you treat them with binding medicines, which does not help; then they should be restrained with a gold thread, for silver wire becomes green and rots, but gold never changes; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of the space between the teeth; and if you see that the teeth are moving, take the thread and double it between the two healthy teeth, then put the affected tooth in the middle of the teeth, if there is one or more, until you feel it touching the healthy tooth on the other side; then continue the covering towards the part where you began, and gently and skillfully restrain your hand until it does not move at all; and let your thread be attached to the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then thread the broken tooth with a thin wire, and twist it together, and place it between the healthy tooth and the gum, so that it does not bleed the tongue; then leave it tight as much as possible, and if it slips, or the wire breaks, then tighten it with another wire; if it holds, it will serve in this way for a long time, and this is the form of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two broken ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is cracked, if it is reset in its place, bit by bit, as we have said; and it does not interfere with anything that is not wise and suffering, and never once is made in the shape of an animal's tooth, and it is placed in the place where the defect is, and it is tightened as we have said, and it holds and serves in this way for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	There is no joint that comes out of the tongue or naturally, which is born thus; or by accident of a wound. And the methods are such that you open the mouth with the tongue, and hold the head in your hand, and lift the tongue; then cover the nervous side of the large, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if it is hard or not, and it is due to a wound, if you boil the herb and cover the large gently; and be careful that the wound is not too deep, for the artery that is outside; and when you have done, lift the tongue with a cloth of rose and vinegar, or of cold vinegar, then put out the tongue a tent of linen; and moisten the sore every night, so that the wounds do not stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs from the wound, apply a glass splinter to the affected area; and if it does not stop, cauterize with a slow-burning firebrand, which is good for the wound; then treat it with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see that the wound is of a brown or black color or hard, and the patient does not feel pain, do not touch it, for it is a chancre; and if it is declining towards suppuration and there is moisture, pour water through an instrument with a thin spatula from one side to the other; and if it does not stop bleeding, apply a glass splinter until it stops, then repeat the process until all blood is removed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never come from within the throat, which are called "godaths", and they are properly called the II mandibles, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healed, then be careful: if they are hard and small and of a pus-like color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron, also for the discharge of blood; but let it stay until it dies, and then you will break it off, or it would break by itself; and if it is of white color and the root is thin, prepare the instrument to cover, but first check if the abscess is at rest and is calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore, place the painful part in front of the sun, and its members should be in a straight position, and the work of the mouth and the prick of the soldiers between his hands, and press the tongue away from all the instruments, of which this is the form; and it should be of silver or fine brass like some knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	If you press the tongue against all these instruments, and you see the abscess, take the needle and the hook in the amber, and draw it out as far as you can; then take nothing with, then cover the instrument, of which this is the form, that seems like a forceps; and throughout the head is curved, and one end the other, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, use a pair of tweezers, which is shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And on one side it is sharp and on the other side it is blunt; and when you have removed one of the arrows, remove the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sharp parts with hot, sharp, and thin water, and if blood comes out, gargle the sharp parts with hot, or cooked pomegranate shells, or mullein leaves, and similar things, until the wound is clean; then care for it until it is healed; and never do arrows ever come out of the throat except the two arrows, so remove them in the same manner as the two arrows should be.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	I treated a woman with an abscess that was lodged inside her throat, namely a small abscess; and she had almost completely closed her throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the conduct that was obstructed, and could neither eat nor drink, and died if she remained thus for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high that it had been placed in two jars through the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I therefore immediately began, and inserted one instrument through the nose, then the tube was passed through a large portion of intestine; then I refilled the other nostril with another instrument, and held the mouth open and pressed the tongue; after inserting the instrument into these abscesses, and drawing out a part, and only a small amount of pus remained outside; thus the woman was able to breathe again through her throat, and began immediately to drink water and wine, and did not cease cutting away at this abscess for a long time; the abscesses grew again and filled the cavity that I had emptied, so that it became very large; therefore I pushed it back in and cauterized it inside her throat: thus she did not grow again; and I left these parts and only God knows what happened to her after me.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When referring to the eye, and it is enflamed and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is not large and round, it is called "uvetta".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help much, and you see that the abscess is calmed, and it is thin, then you must puncture it; and the one that is round and not long; and if it is bloody or dark red or black, then you must avoid incision of the.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger from the pain.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its breadth and length, you should place the hairs in front of the sun, and press the tongue against the instrument that we mentioned earlier; then make an incision in the vein, and remove it, and cover it with one or two of the tools that I mentioned in the incision of the two mandrakes.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you cover only the excess that is beyond the natural end; for if you cover more, it will cause great pain to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we mentioned in the incision of the two mandrakes, and treat it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the pain is too great, then it is necessary to use a cauterizer for the sensation of pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cauterizer is sharp and hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the pain puts its head on your clean hand, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said in the chapter of cauterization, and applies with sharp and live heat, so that it is not too thick or too clear; and in the movement of this instrument, because of which is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the head of the hair or medicine, as the movements of a spoon, and puts the instrument on all the medicine above the uvula; and the pain lies on its side, so that saliva and mucus flows from its mouth through the medicine inside, so that it does not drip down the throat and the blood; then hold your hand on all the medicine and press it on the uvula for a quarter of an hour, until you see the benefit and the medications of the medicine are calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wipe the cotton in the medicine, and boil the instrument through the cotton to the uvula; and do this often, until the cauterizer is perfect, then let it dry for four or five days; and if you have the task of starting the cauterization of the medicine again, start it, and after cauterizing it, wipe it around the uvula with cotton soaked in butter, and clean what is around the medicine; and be aroused by sharp cold, and be treated with gargles until they are healed.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more safe from the incision, than from the cauterization; if it is treated with fumigation in this manner, take chamomile and hyssop and origanum and rue and camomile and similar herbs, and all or some of them in a pot, and put vinegar in it, and make it boil; and the pot should be well sealed with strong earth, and inside the pot have an instrument like a comb in this manner:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or tin, and one of the pricks inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye through the nose, until the eye is dead; afterwards, repeat often, until the eye is dry, and guard that you do not make steam at the beginning of the appearance of the abscess, for many things happen; and do not make steam except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	If this instrument is not present, take a cloth and place it inside the head, so that the tongue does not stick out too much; for the cloth does not cause the vapor to burden the mouth, and it is a good cure together with safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often it is necessary to remove bones or fish spines from the throat, or nothing at all; therefore, you must take out what you can see, and press the tongue against the sun at all times with the instrument, so that you can see the thing; and what does not appear and is returned to the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit the thing as soon as the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps if the thing is removed by vomiting; or the patient has swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of naval, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and tie the sponge to the thread, and then swallow it; and when it reaches the throat, it will stick, and then pull it out; and if it does not come out due to what we have said, take the instrument according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instruments should be curved at the top so that they can more easily enter the throat, and the head should be raised high; and beware that you do not touch the epiglottis, that the tongue does not come, or push the bone inwards; and it is better that the hairs do not bite the instrument, because it is softer or the thing is as such; if it bites down, or pulls it all along the instrument evenly, until it is completely out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the throat's softness
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	There is no softness in the throat, as I said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and if it does not improve, then look at the throat's hairs to the sun, then press the tongue against the instrument that I told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the sinew, then trace it with a small needle, or with subtle needles that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if it does not work, then take a hair, and push it into the neck of the misaligned joint, then push or move the hair with the sharp edge of the iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the misaligned joint is inflamed all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full the cold ash of the inflamed joint, and work the mouth, and pour it in the direction of swallowing, and move it with your hand often; and if soon when the sinew feels the cold, it will be cooled.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If it does not break as we have said, then fog the bad odor of putrefaction with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times, for it will stop without fail.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of the fumigation is that you grasp a pot or one that has charcoal in it, and place a cover over it perforated in the middle, and in that puncture place the instrument; then pour your fumigation, and put the bad odor in the mouth of the snake, and close the mouth, so that the fume does not escape but goes to the lungs; and the lungs will now stop, and if it does not cease, begin the fumigation again many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, and eat salty things and others, and do not drink anything acidic; and then it is the task that it should pass through this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to treat the throat, such as when one can see it, resembles a crooked hook to enter the throat; and it has the shape of a beak, and it has sharpness like lime, so that whatever it takes, it cannot wear out; and this is its form:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapters on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what memory comes after one and another in this book, and they differ in perforation and incision; and it is in two ways that the one is in its own shape itself, and because it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method is for the limbs that are at the waist.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the main part are different from those that come from the foundation, and the abscesses in the shoulder are different from those that come from the joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one should not pierce until the pus is fully drained; and if there are some that it is necessary to pierce as soon as they are ripe, and do not die as soon as they are drained, like abscesses that are beyond joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	When abscesses come from joints, and it is left there until it is surrounded by, perhaps due to corruption of the bone and the nerve of the joint, which is the cause of contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	When the abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay the perforation until it dies, it will harm the main limb; or if it is near the foundation, if you pierce it too late, it will not be able to stand upright, and will remain crooked inside, and there will be a fistula; and it cannot be cured in the long term.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is necessary that you scrape the head of the abscess perforation according to its completion, and this is when the pain is eased, and the departure of the fever, and the lessening of the pain and swelling, and the reduction of the debatement and the relief of the main symptom of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where it is most dependent on the abscess, and where it opens most easily; and let the perforation be long along the body, and if the abscess is near the hands or feet, or in joints and nerves and arteries, and in all equal places where there is no pus.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the position of that member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the limb, it is better to leave the puncture until it is confirmed by completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you puncture it beforehand, it may follow along with the flow of blood from it, and is stained with much feces; and perhaps harden the lips and penetrate deeply into it.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is punctured according to the width of the vein, according to what the limb has need of.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to treat small abscesses, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many cuts according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if such abscesses or it is necessary to cover them with a cloth, and they are softened, then it is necessary to do so as one does with bandages: and if such abscesses are cut in three angles, and if such abscesses are covered like the belly of a mule, as abscesses of arrows; and if such abscesses or they make a round cut, and other cuts and coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	For those who do not have a head, if the abscess is superficial, it is necessary to lance it completely; and if the abscess is large, and there is great swelling, and you lance it, do not draw out all the pus in that hour, but take out part of it; then stop the abscess on the other side, then take out nothing else; do this gradually, many times, until the pus is all out; especially if the wounds are of weak power, or women carrying, or small children, or old men who are decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the experienced never trust the end of the pus, that sometimes the wounds die, and you do not perish.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid therefore this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived your abscess, dry the wound, and see if the abscess wound is small; and if it is a tailor complaining, mollify tents of linen or wool cotton; and if it is large abscesses, and there is much pus, it is necessary that you fill each one with old cotton or shredded linen against moisture, and tie it just above the wound; then open, and treat the dressing until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if there is bleeding in your work, apply sharp cold and cool, and wipe away the blood, and place it on the affected area for many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, apply government and care, and the powders I have mentioned in this book, and if it is very tense, and if the wound or abscess is very painful, then it is best to put on bandages and wipes soaked in wine and oil; and if it is in a state of inflammation, and the wound is charred, then it is best to put on bandages and wipes soaked in cold water or warm water, as we have said; then drain the abscess and dress it and treat it, as it should be, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and see this chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	When small abscesses come from the sores, and are of ways that are in cloths, like the sweat of a horse, and many there are similar.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are also large and such abscesses that have moisture like chicken; and there are some that are hard and stony to cut, and there is no doubt if the artery is not against it.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the abdomen is such that you try every tool called "intercostal", from which the shape comes after, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then do it by lifting up from above the long.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is drained, scrape off without leaving any hair that contains that moisture, for it will return if you leave anything; then put cotton in Egyptian oil, if present; if not, in vinegar and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it there until the next day; and this will continue what is left from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then, as before, restart the cotton, and the second hour, and the third, until you are sure it will not stay all night; then treat the wound with ointment as appropriate, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	If the abscess remains large, then apply the poultice in this form, long; and pour water over it, and scrape off all the skin, and put all your care into drawing out the pus from where it is. And if the artery opposes, do as I told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also do this for the abscess if it is pus-filled, and cut and treat as I told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting above the abscess, if it is more lightweight, as it is made of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or swellings do not have moisture, and among them was the abscess I copied or the swelling of an old woman; and I found the abscess as hard as a rough stone, rough and white, and could not break it; and if one had tried to cut it, one would have made just as much pain as from a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming or swelling, those that come to the head of children and to the roots of the ears, the opening should always be made at the lowest point of the limb, in order to let out the pus; and cure them as it is necessary.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	often abscesses in the neck, and discharge pus from the armpits, and in the groin, and are very painful, and are inflamed together with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	and each scrofula is properly within its side, as with the neck and abscess of the jaw, as we have said; and similar scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are some malignant ones that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one which you see of good disposition in the touchwood, and is similar to the color of the flesh, and motionless from every part and not attached to the nerve or artery or conduit, and not deep; then it is necessary that you cut it from above, and scrape every part, and close the two lips of the wound as one, if you have experience, as we have said in abscesses of the jaw; and peel it slowly and carefully, and be sure that you do not cut the nerve or vein, which the hand does not escape, and do not see too soon, before you close what you do not need.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery, and it does not let you open it, put in the wound vitriol broth, or some powders that stop bleeding, and close the wound; and leave it until the abscess is soothed, and the wound is softened, and then begin to poultice.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the wound is cleansed, return to your work, until you complete it; then ask your guide whether there are any small scabs remaining, if so, cut and remove them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has a vein in the root of the scab that is large, then you should not cut that scab at its root, but tie it with a double-strength thread, and let it drop through it, without harm; then fill the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove all the pus, it is necessary that you gather the two lips of the wound and hold them together, then since there is no remaining excess due to the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	and you should cover the root of it and pull out, and hold as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those abscesses that have excess, perforate where it apertures dead; and perforate thus as the one before said, depending, then apply bandages and similar things, so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is well dressed, apply charcoal ointment until it is healed.
de squinance	of squinting
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and said of the throat-cutter; but I never saw one in our land, and it is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who squint, it is necessary that the edge of the throat, which is called "epiglottis," be avoided; and because all the veins and the root of the evil are in those who have abscesses chock full in the mouth, or in the throat or in the tongue.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the root of the tongue, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the danger of strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to cut the epiglottis, we should cut it outside of three circles or four with a small incision across, between the two circles or by the amount of the incision through the syfac, and not into the cartilage; and those who do so are suitable for the section of the epiglottis that there is no harm, and the vessels are long and do not bleed.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is not careful, it is necessary to stretch the skin of the neck all around, then cut the throat until it reaches the cheneil; avoid the blood vessels of the vein, if you see anything, and then cut the syfac as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream of the cheneil that jumped through the bone that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed for which there is doubt of strangulation, bring together both lips of the wound carefully, and sew it all together without the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause blisters to rise until they are healthy.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely stiff, and the wounds are judged to be dead, and the defect has healed.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then one should cover the epiglottis for this reason that the wounds cannot heal, and he breathes through the wound, and thus is kept from death; and because they ordered the ancients to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease had passed, which passed in three days or four. And then they commanded to sew the wound and cure it, as long as it was healing; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a young lady took a knife and stuck it in her throat, and cut off part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and found her as if she were dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the arrow that had come out of it, and although she had not sucked blood or poured water through her mouth except for her throat, and the blood flowed from the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sutured the wound, and cured it until it was healed; and she did not suffer any harm except that she was hoarse, and returned to her usual state; for I believe in the healer of the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large abscess in the color of a grape, and it is very common in women; and it occurs in two ways: natural, and accidental; or naturally without any cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental way is in two ways: one is similar to a large abscess, and the other way is similar to an abscess that comes from our artery; and there is fear, and it should not be opened except by a small needle, and it proves and searches throughout the entire introduction: if you find it as such, and cannot be drawn out at all, if it coagulates, like how we draw out the large abscess, and it is removed entirely, if there is any; and search for it quickly, and treat it as it should be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	For us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways we have, of which I will say all the similarities; and now it is necessary for me to tell the difference that is between us and extraction.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that extraction is cold and fever-keeping, until the boils are passed, and is accomplished by sweating; then the fever and the cold rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With our way, there is no cold or fever or pain, and it contains the abscess, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins as a small pustule, and becomes large; and they are according to two similarities, whether dry or moist, and many colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When treating a new patient, it is necessary to first examine and try the instrument called "entromissoire" according to its form, as described in the following chapter.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method for examining abscesses is that you press on the wet cloth that you have placed in the abscess, and gradually increase pressure until you feel that the instrument has pierced through, according to the size of the abscess; then remove the entromissoire, and be careful not to cause a burst.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running wound is red in color, make it as I have described for other abscesses; and if after using the entromissoire there is no more running wound, then scrape it off if it is thick, and then cut it into pieces, and scrape off all parts of the skin where it was, and take the cloth away with the patient; and if you cannot take it away cleanly, then cut it off in pieces so that nothing remains.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If there is nothing left, it returns to us many times; and if it stays for a short time without causing harm, then apply some corrosive powders to the wound, close the wound, and place soothing things on the abscess, and treat other ailments until he is healthy; and if it is great, cut out the two lips of the wound, and treat what remains with char.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if it is against you or other, and you are in a hurry, then apply the limb with broken glass, and leave it for two or three days until the wound heals, and rest the blood; then return to the copper that was left behind.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of instruments used for extracting stones, and there are three ways: large, medium, and small; and there are three quarters that are called "albaret", and one that is called "breb", and there are three ways: large, medium, and small, to extract the stones from fistulas; and they are like the needles that one uses for sewing, and they are made of gold, or iron, or silver, and they cost as much as those that are yellow, and they are more effective at removing black pus from fistulas; and they are three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the openings.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of nails are of many similarities, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and there are nails that have two claws in three ways; and there are nails that have three claws, and they are also of three ways; and there are nails that have two claws, and a single claw, and they are also of three ways; and all this is necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The sharpest of these are those that cut from one side only, and there are some that do not cut at all but rather scrape the skin, so that the vein or nerve is not cut; and among these are the needles that are replaced in a loop, so that the pain does not disappear at the opening of the abscess; and they are of three kinds: large, small, and medium, as you see; and one uses only a smaller one in places that are fleshy, such as legs, arms, breasts, and shoulders, and similar parts; and one never uses any other small instrument, resembling the scrapers of pustules, according to this form, to draw blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is placed on no occasion in the wrong place, which is suitable for veins, and arteries, and always returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	No one should inflate the breasts of some men when they begin to rot, as if they were breasts of a woman; and they remain ugly and swollen, and whoever wants to cure them, it is necessary to follow this form of this line from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	then scrape the fat, and fill the wound with medicine mixed with charcoal, then sew the two lips of the wound together, and heal it until it is healed; and if the breast sinks down, and is softened because of its great size, like women, and cut into two pieces above, by the same fissures; so that one holds to the other at the end of one and the other, so that the largest line contains the smallest according to this form, from this line b to the line g; then scrape the skin that is between the two lips, and remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not completely made, because the pain does not want to rest, or because of the escape of blood, then it is necessary to fill the wound with moist cotton in a corrosive ointment; and let it remain until it draws out the remaining fat and the grease, then heal it until it is healed.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the ankles
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from the ankles are hard scrofulous nodes or if they have spines, and there are some that contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, those that contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line b just to line g:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are of similar appearance to scrofula, then treat them as we have said about incising scrofula, and if the wound remains open, then cauterize it as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the breaking of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is broken, and the skin above it is torn, then often abscesses form, and also there is blood in the vein and abscess; and if one knows that it is for the artery, then the abscesses are long and painful; and when you feel it with your fingers, it is stretched; and when it is for the vein, it is red and swollen; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, and especially when it is outside of the bones and joints and neck and mouth of many other places, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to avoid the use of iron, and the one who is at the head should also avoid it, and in the one who is swollen due to arterial blood flowing through the long skin; then open the belly with small incisions, and remove the artery until it is exposed; then insert a needle from one side, and pierce the other side with another needle, and tie the artery with a double thread according to what I have indicated in the extraction of the two arteries that are in the temples; then do not pull the tissue between the two threads of an intravascular device until the missing part is found, and remove the abscess; then treat the wound as advised, until the flesh heals; and if the abscess is for the belly of the vein, it is necessary to stain your hand with what you can get from the abscess on all the skin, then remove the needle from the tissue that you hold in your hand, and pierce, and there should be a double thread, so that you pull it from the other side; then tie the abscess as I have indicated, or with one of the two threads of the needle; and if you doubt that the thread will not go through, then take another needle and draw all the thread of the first needle at the incision of the first needle, and tie the threads in four places; then cover the abscess until the excess is removed, then cover the wound and leave what is tied; then put a piece of moist linen cloth on wine and oil, then treat the wounds and inflammations until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	Similarly, abscesses come in the artery and in the vein, abscesses also come to the nerves when they are cut, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often occurs in the assistants and the two eyes, and in all the places where there are joints, and it is a great abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in many positions with pain; and when one stretches it, if the pain is felt, and it is not inside the body, but outside the skin; and it moves from all parts, and does not go forward or backward, nor up or down, and that which is in the joints does not cover much flesh: perhaps there is contraction; and those who are at the head or face, making the skin to the spasmodic.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, if you have needles, and pierce it at its root; and if it is large, if you suspend it from the spine, and scrape it, then the bone and assemble the wound at the seam, and the cure until it is healed.
des grosses boces pendans	large swellings hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never occurs in the belly and never in any other part of the body, and is a disease called «fungus» by its resemblance to mushrooms, and has subtle roots, and large heads; and there are both small and very large ones; and I saw the man who had two or belly which were more like fungi than anything else, and had no difference, and were white, and had subtle roots, and were cut by moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I copied and found in one XVIII ounces heavy, and in the other VI З., and the work of incision is that you look to see if the hairs are moist, and the color of the arrow is white and moist and of subtle root; if the copper has a wide spatula, and it is present with you the fire cautery.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For in cutting often comes too great spurting of blood, and if you see the hairs spouting and bleeding from the incision of the iron, then take a well-made thread, and tie the arrow as we have said, and leave it for two days; then reset it, and do not stop pulling the thread through until it covers the arrow, and cut through it with work; and if the roots are large, then use the copper itself on the belly, but you must first cover the half, then cauterize so it does not return; then care for the wound, and guard that you do not cover the flesh which is of pale color and poor sense and of little regard.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	This is an abscess that has become infected, and I will come to treat this type of sore later on.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the body is full of blood, it is difficult to move.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.
