If the appearance of the bubo comes from the wound or cut of the groin, and is above the abdomen and in some of the veins, as in other wounds, or of blood that has burst from veins or arteries according to what is before, or of suppuration; and if it is from the rupture of the groin and from the discharge of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the blood, and it is a light thing without pain, and open from various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is for the issue of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it to its two sides, it returns, and if it is torn, and enlarges greatly at the entrance of the bath and for great labor.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when one presses it with their hand, do not constrain much; and if it is for blood, it opens greatly by these signs of abscesses that are large and hard, and is filled with a quantity; and if it is for windiness, it is soft to the touch, and the appearance is whether it is for the blood of the artery or vein or windiness.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you must leave, then let them care for themselves.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often doubt and fear, as I have told you in the chapter on abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if the appearance is for the intestine or the bladder, then it is necessary to command the patient to dye his linen, and to be stretched out straight, then seal all around the bed; then command him to lie still between your hands, then go around the limb that you have marked with the entire length, then stretch half of the abscess above the great umbilical cord; then tie it firmly with a strong thread or a silk rope, and leave the other end loose; then open half of the abscess stretched above the ligature, and insert your finger, and draw out the intestine; if you find the ligature, remove it, and draw out the intestine from the belly; and if you find the bladder, take it at the opening, and remove the excess; and if the artery makes you go against it, or the vein, then go around carefully, then return to your work and take two needles, and insert two threads, and draw out the abscess as you have done in the cross that you will pierce; then stretch the abscess into four parts above the needles, and if you see, remove the needles, and leave the limb until it can heal, and let the dead flesh die by itself; or you can cover it when it has become thin and ready to heal, then treat the limb as we have said; and draw out the pus or moisture that you have found, then treat the limb as it is necessary, and wash the limb.
dou chancre	1. For the fire cautery
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	1. For the fire cautery, we have described in the division the similarities of chancre, and how to treat it with medicines, and how to avoid the cure of iron; and we say that chancre is in the mouth, and great caution is needed in its treatment, and the ancient one says that when chancre is in a place where it can be removed as chancre which is in the breasts, and in the armpits, and in similar places, and all of it should be removed when it is in the beginning; and when it is large and old, if it does not require that you approach it, for I have never been able to cure any. And no one has ever cured any before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the work is in the place where it can be removed, as we have said, it is that you purge once the pain of black bile; then if it has manifest repletion, make the limb clean and dry for the work; then pour your sponges or chalk, and wipe all parts, and bone all parts without leaving anything; and let all blood flow freely, and wipe well the limb with your hand or something, and if the bleeding does not stop, it is contrary to the incision of the artery or vein, so cauterize until the blood is stopped; then cure other ways until it is healed.
de ydropisie	of hydropsy
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the similarities of hydropsy, and in what manner the assembly of the sharp is made, and the signs of each similarity, and the cure that is made by medicines, and that which is cured by iron: if it is only swelling; and one should not touch with iron in these two similarities: that is to say, tympanites and hyposarcoce, for it is a fatal thing; therefore when you treat this similarity of hydropsy which is called «eclites» by medicines, and the cure does not work, if you look if the evils are weak, or if he has another disease besides hydropsy, as all and solution of the belly and similar things; then do not touch with iron, for there is doubt; and if you see the evil of great virtue, and he has no other disease but hydropsy alone, and he is not too old nor too young, then thus: lean the evil straight up your hands, and the ministers press the belly pushing the sharp to the lowest part of the worst, then take the spatula in this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be cutting of two parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be cutting of two parts at the tip, and make sure that it is not too deep so that it does not pierce into the intestines when thrown, and it cannot be bent; then check if there is hydrops near the intestines: if it is for the disease of the liver, then your cut should be on the right side of the third rib three fingers above the navel; and if it is for the gallbladder, then it should be on the left side, and it is not necessary that the hairs grow over the cut so that the superfluous do not run to the weakest part; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and push, and remove your hand from the entire space between the skin and the gallbladder as if scraping at the quantity of an angle or around; then pierce the gallbladder until the space reaches the desired length, and that is the shape of the blade, then pull it out, and do not bend this instrument of which this is the form:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a fine silver chain, and is made of thin brass or iron, and has in its part outside I small perforation; and where it costs one part, III perforations; and II of another part, and I of another; and the patient's tailor cuts it as a pen, and it is the form of the incision that the scribes make on the pen:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top of the instrument is the needle, so that when the instruments come to the edge, if you now draw it downwards over the edge; then remove the middle or third part, for if you remove more than what is necessary at that hour, by chance if the patient dies from the resolution of his spirit due to the weapon, or he faints, or approaches death; but in accordance with the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the wound signify, and its pulses; then remove the instrument and retain the edge, and it is retained now for the one who stops the perforation that is above the syphilitic sore, of which I have spoken, that you prick according to this manner; then start the instrument again the next day, if you see the patient suffering as before, and take a small quantity from the edge; do this every day, and guard yourself against following it too much until it is only a little blood.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt the pain, and you let it be very sharp, then the cure of the sepulture or sand bath, and by much sweating or bathing and in the sun, and if it becomes tanned; and the cure of desiccative medicines until they are healed, and cauterize above the stomach and above the liver and above the spleen after the extraction of the sharp, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the rod
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child ever is born without a wart on the rod, or the wart is small, or it is not in its place.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is necessary to prick at all times with a very sharp needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then put or puncture the very thin thread of silk in the bottom, and tie it and tie it thus for three or four days, and when he wants to urinate, if it is convenient, remove the thread, make him urinate, and then return it; and perhaps it is not convenient, because the urine that comes out does not leave it closed.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the one who is punctured is small, then treat him with a thin thread of silk, as we have said, and it will expand.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the puncture in their joint are blamed, because no one is born with a puncture at the top of the thigh, so that they cannot urinate before their thigh is up; and they cannot urinate because the matter cannot come out of the marsh, and this is a very bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the work is such that the hairs lie evenly on their backs, with the head of the knife and the handle as wide as the tail of a pen, so that the puncture is made in the middle, as it should be; and beware of bleeding which often comes, and if it does, apply the same bandage as for bleeding, and treat the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the pustules of the knife
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Often come boils in the knife, and it is an ugly appearance; and there are both malign and benign ones; if you should prick them at once, cover and clean all of them, then put on a moist Egyptian bandage; then treat the wound until it is healed.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if it is a malignant ulcer, with a putrid color and foul smell, then you must apply cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have cleaned it, and if the ulcer is deep within the flesh and extends inward and outward, then you must first remove the ulcer that is inside; and when it is clean, then treat the part outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you treat them together, do not be sure that the wound of the bone is not pierced, and if it becomes black and corrupt inside and out; then remove everything that is black and corrupted, then apply the ointment made from the skins of grenate pumpkins and vinegar, then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if bleeding occurs, apply the lunar cauterization as follows:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	The cauterizer should aid in the two dispositions: at the time of bleeding and during corruption; and if the pricked part is corrupted and retracted, it is necessary to apply a cotton swab soaked in piss on the wounds and urinate on them; and when the flesh is removed from the head of the stick which has been used for those who have not yet been circumcised, or if it is a wound or an abscess, then it is necessary to scorch it with the instrument of the hair, until the flesh is separated and released from all parts of the stick; and if this is a difficult task, then it is necessary to scorch it with the tip of the stick and the skin, then thoroughly clean between them, and then apply a thin layer of cold linen cloth, so that it does not heal again.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not like other wounds; therefore, when we perform this work of our will, and properly in infants, it is necessary that we do the best work, and the lightest for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not perform circumcision on their children, because they did not use it in their law, and we have only what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of the masters and sages who performed circumcision in the midst, and with force, and at once; if it was not like this, there were two threads, and by chance if one cut above and the other below, it would delay the other.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or the recovery is prolonged, and the pain is doubled, and the wound dressing that is not secure at the point of the member; and the wound dressing of the joint by chance escapes the knife, and corrupts the work, and often they are born thus that they have no need of dressing and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the wound dressing that is made with force to all the length of the thread, I have found the benefit of the experiment, because the forces cut as well above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you press your hand, it cuts equally in all the length of the thread; but let the thread be well stretched around the skin; and let the manner of the first work be that you make the child think, if he listens, that you are not doing anything but tying the thread around the stick only, and then throw it in all kinds of ways that you can; then put your hand straight on the stick and blow on it or kiss, and take it up high until the part of the stick is clean; then clean it well of the dirt that is gathered, then tie the limb with a double thread, then tie it on the other side; and let it rest in your pouch and at the second lesson to the pouch and the index finger, and bind between the two limbs, then lift the stick up hastily and take the head of the stick; then let the blood drip slowly and slowly, for that is the most dangerous; and put powder on it and on the powder a plaster made of one egg cooked in honey, boiled with rosewater blended with fresh oil, and leave it on until the next day, and cure the other wound as long as it is healed.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of forces for the mummification is as follows: the two arms should be stretched and thin, and the hands should be equal to the main hand.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mummification is when the incision is made inside; therefore, you should extend it to your angle, also the copper, and if you cannot hold it at your angle, then tie it with nails, and then the copper.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three days, and what is outside the rod is swollen, let it remain until the abscess is healed, and the skin is lightly scraped; then the copper as you can move it, and guard from the part of the rod, it will not harm.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure therefore the limb of things unclean wound of powder, which we have said or treat of powders, and if one has too much care, it goes above, if it does not harm; cure therefore as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retention of urine is due to oppression of the stone, or of blood frozen, or of bowel, or of charred, or of similar things, which we have said in the division; and if the urine is not released, and you see that the retention by the stone which is high or col of the bladder, then it is necessary to lift the hairs above their knees; and they are placed on the feet on the back, and extend his belly from the part above the back, and constrain the hairs as much as he can; and therefore the belly of the bladder is pressed against the stone above, for which reason the urine is released, and if it does not come, as we have said, and the hairs feel great pain, then it is necessary to administer extraction with all the instrument called «siringue», of which this is the form: and it is of thin silver hair, like the pen of an owl; and it is of a palm length and half, and it is thin at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And the manner of the issue of urine is such that you take a double thread, and tie the head of the thread to the top of a piece of wool or cotton, and fill the tube with the thread; and cut off the excess of the wool and fill it with oil and butter and egg yolk, and make the patient sit on a stool, and the arse the urine and the stick of oiled and olive oil and vinegar; then put the tube lightly in the stick, until it reaches the root of the stick, then double the stick over on top of each other; then fill the tube before with the stick, and the patient feels the urine coming out of the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order except by those who lead or go there because it is twisted; then stop the thread at every little piece of wool and the urine follows the wool, then extract it far, and correct the urine; and start again the tube until the bladder is empty and aligned with the patient.
des maladies de la vessie	of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When skin or blood comes into the bladder, or putrefaction and is gathered, and you see it distill acidic and medicinal substances, then use all the tool called «clepsedre», and this is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the threads by which the medicine cuts so that it stops well the urethra, so that they can draw out the moisture, and put as much as necessary; and when you see your medicines entering the bladder, put the head of the clyster in the moisture, and bring to the opening which is below; if you draw the moisture to the opening, and then close it strongly; the moisture will enter below, and come to the bladder now, so that the patient feels it; and this is the form of the subtle clyster with which one clysters the bladder:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or of lead, and is the highest of the patient's chest; and remove it from where the ribs meet; then take a sheep bladder and put the moisture that you see clisterizer the bladder, then place it between the two breasts formed by a good double thread, and heat the poth over the fire; then pour the head of the clistere into the rod, then strain your hand on the bladder all around the moisture, until the patient feels that this moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then tighten the thread strongly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dough, and put inside what you see oil and moisture and vinegar, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, of pressing with your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have mentioned in the division the methods of stones and extraction together with medicines; and I have said the difference between a stone that is embedded as rain, and all signs, and in which stone one should open with a drill; and in the bladder, and in the staff; and I will tell you clearly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone that is embedded in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the sharp pain of the bladder is similar to sharp pain in its subtlety; and it opens quickly, and causes great pain to the staff, and it can happen many times, and then returns; and at too many of these jumps, the foundation; and it is light for the healing of children until they are four years old, and it is very grievous in elders, and it is constant in those who are between young and old; and it is a lighter cure for those who have large stones, than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, it is first necessary to cleanse the wound with cloth, to draw out all the filth that is in the entrails.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never blocks the way to seek the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound by the feet, and stand up and move it away from the body, so that the stone descends to the edge of the anus, and never goes up through the thigh; then place it between your hands, prepared, and your hands are away from your thighs, so that the anus is completely inclined downwards; then remove and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hurry now to cut across the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if she does not cry out at all, then prick your right index finger with an oil-soaked needle, if the pain is sharp, or your middle finger, if the pain is dull; and place it in her foundation, and press the stone, and when you feel it at your finger, then moisten the neck of the bladder; then press upwards, and the stone will come out where you saw it cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the midwife to press the bladder with her hand, and command her to extend her right hand over the genitals, and her left hand to remove the skin that is outside the genitals in the part where the incision is made; then cut the spatula-shaped stone, which is the shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	When between the bones and the base, not in the middle but on the right side of the nave sinister; and the straight should be above the stone, and the tail should be at the foundation or below, and the tail should be narrow on one side and wide on the other according to the quantity of the stone, not too large; perhaps the pressure that is at the foundation, that it may not jump out of place; and if there are pieces of stone or angles, and margins: if it is greasy to issue; and if there are pieces that are soft, similar to a gland, and rounded, from which the issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	If there are angles and margins where it is, make the incision wider; and if it does not jump, it is necessary to strain it with nails that are as thick as a lime at the head, to prevent the stone from escaping; or you can use a subtle hooked instrument at the head; and if you cannot engage it thus, enlarge the pore slightly, and if there is no decortication, then strain it with vinegar; and if there are more than one stone, first strain the largest at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then remove the smaller ones, and the others afterwards if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very large, it should be made larger, and a larger wound should be made.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the wound: either it dies, or the urine comes out through the opening that the sutures cannot hold; but no matter how hard you try to pull it, or to tear it with pliers, until you tear it into pieces; and when you have completed your work, apply envelopes of incense and aloe and dragon's blood to the wound, and bind it, and place a moist cloth on top of it in oil and wine, or in oil and vinegar and cold vinegar, to soothe the abscess; then close the wound over its collar, and do not remove the bandage until the next day.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you reset it, rise the joint well with oil and vinegar, then treat with ointment and basilicon until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if an abscess comes into the wound and corrosions, and clots of blood in the bladder, and it is held back by the urine, which is known to be withheld without causing pain: then bandage the wound, and extract that blood, for if it remains, it will rot the bladder, and cause harm; then lift the wound with vinegar and salt and oil, and help in all ways you can until it is healed; and it is necessary that all the ointments you use, that you tie the two thighs together, and gather the medicines above the wound.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the arrow is small and it is conducted with a stick, and tied up, and the urine cannot come out; then according to what I have said before, you must cut it many times, or excuse the cut for this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have experienced this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take a piece of iron according to this form and be at three corners tied up in one thread:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the stick outside of the arrow, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then lightly boil the iron in the stick until it reaches the arrow; and gradually turn the iron in your hand on the other side of the arrow, until you can pierce the arrow from the other side; if urine comes out immediately, then press your hand above what is remaining of the arrow that is inside the stick.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is already broken, and has sprung forth with the urine, and is sharp among the hairs; and if you cannot do this for any reason, then take a thread from one side of the stone and from the other, then make the rod in the middle of the stone between the two threads, then extract it forcefully, and remove the thread, and clean the clotted blood that is in the wound; and treat it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It rarely happens that a stone is inserted in women, and if it ever does happen, the treatment is difficult, and is forbidden for three reasons: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who is well-kept and willing to expose herself to shame, specifically when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that perhaps one cannot find a woman well versed in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that if the woman's stone is larger than the man's stone, it is necessary to make a deeper incision, and there is great fear involved. And if necessary, it is necessary to seize a skilled midwife, and point out the truth to her, and if you do not point out the truth, then it is not necessary to perform the operation; and present her with a safe knife in the life of women, or a woman who knows part of the art, and command her to do what you command during the examination of the stone; and look very closely if the woman is virgin: therefore, it is necessary to place her foundation or basis and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, she constrains it outside her basis, and recommends that she place her foundation or with the pain, and press her right hand firmly on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she finds it, she must move it from great to great, from the entrance of the anus to the root of the thigh; then cut into the bone at the root of the thigh against the middle of the thigh, where it is muscle-covered, and feel the arrow in that part; and do not move her body above or below the arrow, and let the tailor make a small hole in the first place; then sew up the wound, if you sense the arrow so sharp that the wound cannot be closed until the arrow can be removed, and know that many kinds of arrows are: namely, small and large, sharp and blunt, long and round, and those with rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if you recognize the similarities to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if you do not know, apply a piece of broken glass to the wound, and hold it there for an hour until the wound is cleansed; then return to your work, until the arrow is fully removed, and have the instruments I mentioned in the extraction of the arrow help you in your work; if you do not know, and it is the artery that is cut, apply powder on the wound and bandages and ointments, and do not start again, and leave the arrow and do not pull it out, lest by chance the patient dies; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood is calmed, and the wound has healed, return to your work until the bone is firm.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carcinoma
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing other than the assembly of moisture or white sac, which is detached from the intestines, which contain the urine; and it is called "sac", and never is properly in the bladder of the urine, if one wants that it be another bladder; and this is the skin of the intestine between the white sac that we have said; and it does not have a pouch without.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the growth of this branch is due to weakness that comes from the base, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And sometimes it comes from the base, and this moisture has many colors: or it is a declining yellow to jaundice, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and there are more; and these are the signs of knowing this assembly, because if it is white and flat as we have said, it is the abscesses, and not long since, like the shape of an egg, and does not open the joints, because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if it has moisture in its own skin, it is the abscesses with part of the egg, and because of this people think it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joints and the white yellow, then it feels bad; therefore when you see the color of the moisture, examine all the surroundings to find out why it has that shape before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the intromission, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When we treat it with iron, it is necessary to clean the hairs according to the power and repletion of his body; then place him on his back, on something quite high, and cover him with much cloth; then bend over his right side, and command the minister to bend over his left, and extend the knife to one of the two ribs near the spine; then take the spatula and scrape the skin of the ribs from long to above the knuckle, and make your cut straight across the skin of the ribs just below the white face, and scrape the skin subtly according to the power; then pierce the white plain with a sharp and wide hole, and remove all the sharpness, and then put your forceps, and press the white face up; and do not touch the ribs except the white face itself; scrape the entire side of him subtly, if you do not scrape it well, it will return to the sharpness; and if the sharpness springs up at your work, then reset it in its place when you have completed the work of the white face; then sew the two edges of the ribs together at a seam, then treat it as the other wounds, until it is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you try to heal the wound that has been corrupted by another disease, it is necessary to tie the vessels that are suspended, doubting the flow of blood; then cover the wound with a dressing that is suspended, and extract the wound, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the bone is assembled in two parts together, since it is two branches; then cover the other part as you have done the first evenly, then suck out the blood, and put on the wound a cloth moistened with rose oil; and put on top of that another cloth moistened with wine and oil, and place two bandages over the two covers, and tie it above the limb that is in this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two cloths, and place them according to this pattern and gathered together by sewing in the neck of the breeches, and the one of the patient taken above the foundation just below the back, and the other at the part of the wrist; and the other head above the two angles, and all assembled the restriction in the loop of the breeches; and never is medicined this branch of cauterization in place of iron tail, and it is that you take one cauterizing needle fine, and cover the skin of the wounds, and it is heated as we have said, so that the white pus that contains the sharp is revealed; then take the cauterizer according to this form, and pierce that pus with short strokes, and the skin with this fine cauterizer:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And in all ways that you can, until you remove everything; and guard that the fire does not touch the eye; and cleanse this work so it is safer; and beware of blood clotting, and bleeding or other things, if anything goes against you, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	If the pain is not severe, and does not want to endure this work due to its horror, then use perforation as I told you; so when you are certain by the signs that we have said that the sharp object is laid aside, then place the pain on the raised seat; then pierce the abscess at the part that is away from everything widely, and put the perforation at the length of the body; and make the openings wide so that all the sharp point flows out; then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and let the remaining sharp point heal; then treat the wound until the wound is healed; and if the white cloth does not let the sharp point issue from the mouth of the wound, then you must use a pen or the instrument that treats the sharp point of hydropiques, because its form is as before; and expand the wound, and make sure that the sharp point returns, and is assembled after six months or more, and when it is assembled as before, and thus the pain will pass its days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of abscess of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	There are many positions in this section that seem to me to be better left alone, and I will tell you about the work and similar things of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	Therefore, many abscesses come from wounds, and even in the testicles; and this is often the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to say from excessive acidity and cold, which is spread in the testicles, or from impact; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the blood; and it does not cause pain, and it is a grievous abscess; and perhaps some grayish, pus-filled, and yellowish abscesses come from a wound in an artery, or from inflammation of the vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by the artery, it is known by the appearance of an abscess, when you press it to your fingers; and it should only be touched if necessary.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Those who are made of blood drawn from a vein are known by their appearance of gentle touching of the fingers, and can often make a cut above this resemblance, and on other parts; and it is that you should care for the wounds, then put the end of the thread in the top, and pull out the thick white sinew, and deliver the suspensor from all parts of the wound.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the wound is already sore with these charges, then it is necessary to cut the wound and care for it; and if it is in the sinew, or in what is inside the veins, then it is necessary to remove all of that and care for it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the shoulder is behind the neck, then it is necessary to cover it completely, and straighten the neck, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your surgeries are completed, apply the wound with a soft cloth in rose oil and wine, then use other treatments until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the groin
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is a kind of abscess surrounded by an envelope similar to a blister, with the softening of the groin, and the pain increases when it moves; and the treatment of this disease is as difficult as the previous one, and we will tell you the work of this in accordance with what the ancients did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary to sit the painful joint on the highest seat, then hang the suspensory ligament of the fingers down to your fingertips, and all the tendons that are close to the wrist, and tie them with the masters, and extend them properly; then cut the spatula sharply across the middle of the tendons, as far as they are covered, and then scrape from each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in the temples; then take a needle or double thread, and tie it to the first bone where the blood came out, and tie the other end to the other head; then align them straight in the middle of the body, according to the length of the body, and cut through the corrupted veins; then cure the wound as with the others, so that none of the tendons are cut; for by this no harm comes, and if all the tendons come out, it is necessary to pull the tendons from all the tendons; so that the eye does not lose its sight due to the incision of the tendons, and they dry up and cannot be helped.
de la routure dou syfac	of the toothache
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The causes of this branch are from the section that comes out of the toothache, or from the extension on the stomach in the part of the inguinals, because the intestines descend from that toothache to one of the groins; and this toothache is either from the section of it, or from the extension of it, and these two ways of many causes come: from percussion, or from jumping, or from shouting, or from lifting heavy weight, and similar things; and the signs when it is from the extension of the toothache, are that it comes little by little, in long tension, and does not come suddenly; and it is the abscesses equal up to the pubic bone, because the toothache approaches the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it comes to the section of the tooth, which brings on sudden pain at the beginning, and is accompanied by various appearances of abscesses outside the skin, and it is for the outcome of the intestine and the heart due to the decay of the tooth.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never with the intestines, and they are retained inside, and cause great pain to suffer in the patient, especially when pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these cures of iron, for which one must be careful not to touch.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the method of the work is that you command or pain to twist the intestine into your hand inside the wound, if it can be retracted; then place the neck above and between your hands, and loosen the jaws; then hold the head above, and cover all the skin of the belly with cloths according to what you have skill for opening the wound; so that the pus can come out; then scrape the tooth that is outside the skin of the belly, until the white tooth is completely exposed from all parts; then insert your index finger in the direction of the belly, between the white tooth that is outside the skin of the belly, and between the second tooth, and behind the belly, and between the second tooth; and move the tooth with your left hand inside the belly, and hold the white tooth high in your right hand, and loosen the belly towards the tail; and command the assistant to stretch the belly upwards, and remove what is behind the bandage; and if you find anything, if it is not intestine or white tooth hard, and if you find anything, insert it into the stomach outside; then take a needle or a thread made of twelve threads of wool, and insert it in the back part of the tooth, which is after the skin of the belly; afterwards the tail, then cover the threads with cloths, as long as there are four threads; then form them into the shape of a cross, and hold the tooth, which we have said is outside the skin of the belly, from two thick threads; then wrap the threads in two thick threads, so that none of the vessels that they may touch can enter into the wound, as we have said before; and finally place the first thread according to the round shape that the belly bears; then cover the part which is outside the skin of the belly, as we have said before; then apply soft linen in oil to the wounds, and apply the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never cauterize the white swelling that we have mentioned after incision, due to doubt of bleeding.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this has happened many times, and leave the thread in place until it heals through it; and if it takes too long to fall off, then roast with sharp hot iron, and put on what we have said, until it heals; then cure the wound with other cures, until it is healed perfectly.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carbuncle
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure by iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made in a manner similar to the branch that is together with the viscera, in a way that you tie the vessels, after the cut slightly above the bone; then cover in and cure the abscess with what works, until the vessels heal; and the cure as we have said, until it is healed perfectly.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never come out of the joints as we have said, and open them wide; and let no one touch the intestines with their fingers, and if they do, it is little, and repair every hour; and in any case, if it remains too long at this point, the wound or swelling believes that the intestine is sending; and this happens by the extension of the swelling which is at the joints, as we have said, because it is stretched, then it is softened and inflated the intestines and opened; and the cure is by cauterization, as we have said before; and it is that the hairs are placed so often on their back between your hands, then cover the wound of the rupture inflated with the large according to the quantity of three fingers; and then draw the swelling which is outside the skin that covers it, then take the tail and put it on the wound of the swelling; and press against the front of the belly, then cut the two intestines appearing above the tail, and both; then draw the head of the tail, and do not cover the swelling or extend the skin or anything else, as I have told you in the cure of the intestines; then treat the wound.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the tendons, if you uncover and heal the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ligament is tightly stretched, and does not appear in the fracture, and the cauteries are quiet in this place, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the boots
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the leather of the boots is softened in some men, because the charcoal inside is softened, and it is visible; and it is a matter, when one wants to cure it, that one makes the pain lie on top of his back, and cut the softened leather over the natural leather; then gather the two edges to one seam, and if you see, first remove the excess softened leather at three or four seams; then sew between the seams, and cure it as with other wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.
dou chastrement	forcibly
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	Forcibly, it is commonly used in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and there are only two ways for which it is necessary: one is that the patient responds forcibly when asked, and forcibly undergoes treatment; and the other, because we often have need to forcefully handle some animals to help us, such as a goat and a sheep and a cat and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I therefore say that forcibly is done in two ways: by traction or by cutting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one that we do by traction, we make the animal sit in hot water until the muscles are softened and warm; then take them in your hand, until they are returned and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.
