For the chastening of the waist: it is necessary that you blacken the beast, and press the leather of the belts in your right hand, then tie the suspensor, and cover each eye with a cloth, when you have well burned them; and leave no drop of the sensitive sap and the subtle sap which is on the vessels; and this way of chastening is more effective than that made by attraction, because at attraction something of the belts remains, by which the beast desires luxury. Then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	des hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermofrodie is found in two ways among men: one is that between the two thighs, open as wide as the natural figure of a woman, with hair and sometimes cutting into the urine.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is found in women, and has a penis like a stick and two thighs.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for men and women is that you cut off all the infected flesh, and treat them as other wounds; in the second way, of men whose urine sprays through the skin of the thighs, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the tenting
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tenting device is a sharp object placed above the natural part, as long as it is too ugly to see; and some women have had it as large as a hand, and that is the treatment.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to clean the excess of the tenting device with your hand or tweezers, and gently remove it; and do not pull too much in front, because blood does not come out, then treat other wounds until it is healed; and for another char that is born at the mouth of the marsh, and use it, and by chance it jumps out, and it is according to the appearance of a cow, and because of this they called the old «cow disease».
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary to put it back, as we have said about the tendon, and care for it until it is healed.
de erratique	For the shoulder dislocation due to moist
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratic if is when the nature of the woman is not well perceived, or the pulse is small; and it is natural by birth, or accidental by disease that has come to be; or it is caused by a sharp injury, or a subtle or sharp poison, and is made in the marsh, or in the ribs, or outside, or wherever it may be; and they differ in conception, and childbirth, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this is by the look of the body.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	When the swelling appears to be near the surface, it is best to apply your fingers or a spoon.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is a subtle swelling, and it is near the two lips, then hurry, and do as follows: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back, spreading her legs; then stretch the two lips, until the subtle swelling is removed, and it is over the swelling; then take linen, and dip it in oil, and place it on the affected area, and bind it to the woman every day, so that she cannot move.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the swelling is hard and sharp, then it is best to apply a soft cloth like a leaf of myrtle.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is from a horse kick, if it is lifted up and covered; and have the medicines steeped in blood, such as dragon's blood, incense, and abundant amounts of wine; then apply a wide piece of cloth so that the wound cannot close; and thus leave it open for a long time, and then apply a tent of dry linen; then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the marsh there is a horse kick wound, if it needs to be covered, do so in this manner, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the abscess that is in the marsh, one should not touch with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that usually do not bleed, and when hemorrhoids become old, they become thrombosed; and we have said in the division the similarities of those, and the signs, and I will say here those that require treatment.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I said that hemorrhoids and thrombosed veins, when they are first formed in the marsh, and do not appear until felt, if not treated with iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that can be felt at the edge of the marsh are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore it is necessary to put the woman in a cold house, then the thrombosed vein with pliers, and the copper at its roots, then powder over medicines restricting blood, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then boil her feet for an hour, then put her in very cold water; and if blood flows out, sit her in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gentian and similar things, and then take wheat flour, and make a poultice with honey and egg on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is stained, it is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him sweat by applying suction cups to his back and breasts; then take the linen, and soak it in juice of plantain or juice of agrimony with old wine, and apply to the limb.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is ready to burst, treat the limb with poultices until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red, and resembles a harsh callus, if it should cover it as I have said of the thistle; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	of boils from the marsh
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Many ways of boils come from the marsh, such as chancre and pus-filled abscess and herpes and estiomenes and fistulas and hemorrhoids and pus-filled boil, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I must mention in this treatment the boil that comes from the marsh, which is not among the boils that blister; and if you know how to treat with iron, look at whether the boil is aggravated at the beginning of its coming, and painful and feverish, and if it becomes red, then see.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not rush to pierce, but make him wait as long as the pain is eased; and then place the injured part on a chair, and have two small stools where he can lean, and support it on his back, and bring his feet to the sides of the leg; and let his knees be spread, and put his arms away from his knees, and tie them together with a good rope; then place the bandage over his right side, and have the tool ready that is used to open the mouth of the wound, because after this comes the forming; and it is necessary that when you see this tool being applied, that you check the depth of the wound, so that what goes into the wound does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the injured part; and if the tool is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the tool does not hurt the injured part; and it is necessary for him to put the horn of the tool on top, and to stain the tool.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is open, and it is done with the hand roughly, if it needs to be covered at the head, cover it with the spatula of lead; and when the wound is empty, it is necessary to put moistened lint in the wound with rose oil or dry vinegar; and place the tent from the wound to the back of the marsh, and place above the marsh and above the other clean moistened lint with hot or boiled mustard; then cure after two hours of ointment applying to it, until it is healed; and never lift the marsh and the wound by a poultice of boiled eggs and honey, and then boiled or rooted lily and aristolochia longa are cooked; then reapply the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is stitched in the marsh, then it is necessary to be careful not to cook with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Midwifery is first in the delivery that she knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs when you see the woman approaching, and wants to smell the ar: then hasten the infant to issue; then scrape that childbirth is according to the natural figure, and is the second with him; and when you see these signs, it is necessary to gently press his belly, so that the infant issues soon; for when it issues from its head, the second is with it, and is buried in the marsh by good cleaning; and this which comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes above its feet, and comes from the back or the shoulder, and the hands, or it comes above its belly, or sometimes, and is turned over by chance onto its neck, and by other bad shapes; so it is necessary for the bailiff to be wise and subtle in these things, and if she goes wrong and is deceived, I will show you all the figures as to how one should help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out of its head naturally, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then let the midwife sit on a seat, or the women hold her; and rub her with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then give the midwife between her two fingers the smallest spatula:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	and pierce the second joint, and copper to its angle as far as the moisture that is now correct; and take the belly of the woman until the child descends, and if it does not, then it is necessary to clyster the woman with a decoction of fenugreek with oil of cumin; then let her drink and vomit it down, and keep her mouth and nose closed for an hour: if this now brings forth the child.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands are dislocated, it is necessary to reset them gently and gradually; and if they cannot enter, then place the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up; then lower the chair to the ground, and tie the woman, so that she does not fall during the lifting; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then cut open the abdomen which was previously opened, and extract the child, and reset it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	from the issue of the child above its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes up to its feet, then it is necessary to put it on top; and then slowly turn it and turn it, until it is even; then take both feet and extend them slowly and slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	If it jumps up to the knees, then command it to grab, and let it spit out the condition; if it jumps farther, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, then slowly turn it and turn it, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Because then it is completely straight.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	If it does not come out as we have described, take a handful of high-quality oak sawdust, and oil of savory, and melted gum, and grind everything in a mortar; and put on the natural form of the woman inside and outside this bandage, then make her sit upright until above the ribs; and when she is softened from above, make her a mustard poultice, and put it on, and leave it for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her vomit and hold her mouth and nose, and lightly press her belly, for the child is now born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	from the issue of the child upon its knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if you put the blanket under its hands; then place it on its back, and hang its feet down, and let it lie on the bed; then gently fold its hands, and take its hands over its belly, and remove its cussins until it is clean from below; and if the child does not move, take its feet and gently move its belly upwards, then push your hands under its belly; and slowly bring the child up; and gradually feed the child.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the birth of a child who comes out wide with one hand extending
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	It is necessary to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, lift the woman, and go; if she cannot go, I make her lie on the bed, and stretch out her legs; then relieve the muscle that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, I make her sit on the chair, then study to bring back the hand; and as the child, according to the natural figure, and I command it to breathe until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of a child on its neck, and it has extended its hands, and its face turned towards the back of its mother
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary that the bleeder wash his hand, then slowly and gradually turn it over, and lightly rub it; and when it is even, if it is muscle-bound and stiff, as we have said, then make her move slowly and gradually; and when you have done this, make her sit on the seat, and command her to defecate; and make her evacuate.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner, for all the other limbs.
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to doing this for all the other limbs, if the second person cooperates with your hand, until the moisture is drained; and if the infant's head and neck can be covered with a cloth, do not retain it, and make the child breathe; then feed the child inside, as you wish, and command the woman to defecate once: then it is easily done.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is often the case that twins are born, and sometimes they are born three or four at a time; and this is not an uncommon thing, and it happens quite often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	It is strange that they do not live, unless they are named; I know why they are multiplied, and are separated by the suture which binds them together, which is called the septum; and sometimes they are born as naturally as any other child, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born very badly, as we have said the care should be, and if the afterbirth is subtle, and it does what it is supposed to do quickly and gently, then it should be done in such a way that it is beneficial for their health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	None are formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth, seventh, or more than fifteen, and all are formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the skilled physician, and it is necessary that the bailiff should know everything, because by chance similar things happen to him; so do accordingly as it is necessary.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you are treating the woman of the dead child or belly, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to handwork; if the woman is of sound virtue and has no accident or fear of death; then it is necessary that you should know whether the woman is lying on her back, and her arms leaning down, and her legs raised; and the midwife should use two fingers, or she is tied to the bed so that she is not treated for the delivery of the child; then wipe the mouth of the mother with oily moist cloths with mustard and fenugreek and linseed, then put the midwife's hands in these oils and these mustards; then apply them lightly to the mother, then if she bites the instruments that are suitable for her, and if the child is wrapped in a blanket that is appropriate, and if it is not apparent that it has descended over its head; then put the instruments in her eyes or her collar or her mouth or in her palate or behind the beard or in the forehead or on the ribs, and if it has descended over its feet, then put the instrument in one of these places that we have said, until the thing is empty; and this is the shape of the instrument:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then flip the other side, where you have skill, so that the extraction is even; and then place it evenly by moving from one side to the other, to make it come out, and let the teeth hold, as in this form:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, use some of its own oil, and push it into that part, and pull out the other part; and if none remains, put this tooth or more on top of the shoulder, and do this as much as it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes in front of the other, and it cannot be brought back by tightening, then you must wrap it around the bandage until it comes out completely; then put it in the joint of the foot or on the ankle, and so you should do in the other hand, and on both feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the question is about a child who is large and has a narrow outlet, or if the head is very high, it is necessary to use the spatula with spines between your fingers, and straighten the head; or you can use the instrument called «almidach», which comes with the tools of the chapter that follows this one; and do the same for a child with a large natural head; then remove the bones with pliers, and if the question is about a fracture, hold it firmly until the blood stops flowing; and if the blood cannot be stopped, cut pieces of cloth to plug the wound; and if the child is swollen in the belly or on the sides, it is necessary to pierce it until the blood flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the infant is lying on its feet, then light traction and gentle pressure to the marsh of the mouth are appropriate.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if the infant is lying on its back or belly, it is appropriate to gently pull the blanket wrapped around it; and when the stomach or belly is opened, remove all the moisture until there is none left; and if the other limbs are also frozen, and the patient remains unconscious, then apply warmth to the mouth from the marsh, and draw it towards the mouth; then apply I or II, and pull it out; and if the mouth is retracted due to an abscess that has formed, do not force it, but instead treat things that are moist and greasy; and apply ointments, and use astringent, moistening, and softening agents.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the shoulder is dislocated above its joint, and you can put it back in place, follow what we have said about the living child; and if there is no means to do so, then try to realign it by pieces, and leave nothing of the second part.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, follow what we have said about abscesses that come in the marsh; and if blood comes out, it should be immediately stopped with tight bandaging, and other treatments should be followed.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had died, then consulted the other about it, and refused to let the others die.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, some abscesses appeared in the throat, and they swelled so much that they burst, and began to cause great pain.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went to the doctor, and he thought for a long time, and could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I placed strong adhesive on it, and some bones stuck to it, and after some time, others did as well.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly does not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I saw the wound, and in it were many bones, until the woman was much better; and I saw the woman in such a way for a long time, and it remained a little blood in the wound; and I did not remember this chapter except because when the masters find an unusual thing, they know how to provide help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	bring the marsh back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Here comes the second form of pressure, where we apply books; and to the second question of the second joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Indeed, the corners should be more subtle than the restrictor, and made of flat or boxwood; and the mouth of the fist should be two inches wide, and the edge of the trees one palm and a half long; and between the two joints should be two additional wedges of this same wood, which are firmly inserted into each other, half a palm or a little more in length; and these two wedges are placed in the mouth of the marsh to open when turning the two corners.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, should be made of flat iron or boxwood, according to the appearance of pliers; and it should have two prongs, as you see, one palm long, and two wide; and when you want to open the mouth all at once, place the woman on the bed, the feet together and the legs apart, then push the two prongs together into the mouth, and hold the chief of the instrument between her teeth; then work your hand with the instrument equally, according to the quantity you want to open the mouth of the woman, until the bone does what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This instrument is always above them, and there are many of their kinds; and when the eyes have them arranged, the more hasty the work, and the higher for people in quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If you do not disregard this instrument because its need is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second instrument is held back from childbirth, it is necessary to command the pain to hold its womb, and then make it expel the condition, and hold your hands on the mouth and nose; and if she sneezes through that, well done.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, if she has the pot, and make a steam or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the marsh, such as rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, should be cooked or boiled over the fire; then put one pot or steam in the mouth of the marsh, and the other at the top of the mouth, and let her sweat until the vapor goes inside the mouth; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint moves out of place.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains in place after this treatment and is not too tight, command the patient to massage their right hand with oil of sesame or mustard plaster, and then apply it naturally, and find the second joint; and when they have found it, grasp it and extend it gently and gradually, so that the tendon does not tear during extraction; but move it slightly to the right and left, and then remove it; if it comes out and disappears.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the marrow of the bone is already thin, we have said the treatment of expectoration and fumigation of herbs; and if none of these things are present, then do not try to pull it out; but it is better that what is at the marrow of the bone, that you tie it to the woman's wrist, then counter-irritate with a tetrapharmacon ointment; so it will heal and be strong; but nevertheless, when it does come out, there comes bad smell to the stomach and head, and causes pain.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, then use these concoctions for the nose: none of the ancients have experienced the fumigation of celery and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument used for fumigation in women with retention of menses and the secondine is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is similar to a needle, and one puts the tip subtly into the natural passage, and the others wide above the fire; and let the fumigation be over the coals, and the tine until it is burned out, and then start another one.
de percier lou fondement	of piercing the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not pierced the foundation, but rather it has been stopped by some subtle swelling: therefore, if necessary, one must first pierce that swelling at its proper place, and not pierce the space aguishly, and stitch the wound so that it does not touch it; then put on a moistened cloth with wine and oil, then the treatment of ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not reset, place a splint on the joint and let it rest for some time, and it should be stiff as the child wants to go into the chambers.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never does a swelling of pus from a wound or an abscess come; if it comes, cover the wound: if it is treated, as we have said of the splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the deep fistula
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from outside the foundation are nodular and thicker than those that come above the foundation or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when that nodule is old, it works, and becomes moist with white or subtle pus, and never are these fistulas permanent; and they are known by the fact that there is egestion or ventosity when the pain makes egestion, and perhaps some verses.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if there are fistulas that perforate the bladder, and perforate half of the penis; and they reach the joint of the thigh, and perforate the buttocks.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows the fistula passing through the basement, and not passing: and it is that you should bore your finger or basement, and insert a thin needle of silver or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has twisting, if you bore a thin tent of lead, or horsehair, until you feel the tent or hair at your finger; and if you do not feel it, and there is no purulence, edema, or vermin, as we have said: save that it does not perforate further; then hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula is persistent near the bladder or near a urethral conduit, if it allows urine to pass, and cannot be healed by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perforated near the hip joint, then the tendon is close to the bone; if there is no twisting and the pain is internal, then it is already in place, and there is no cure by medicine or by cauterization; and in these persistent fistulas, there is no other cure than labor, and the vanity of those who attempt them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not persistent and not ancient, in hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the pains are hidden between your hands on its back; and the legs are raised up to its knees, and its knees are bent towards its belly; then boil a tent of lead, or of pitch if there is twisting, until you remove the tent.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the pain is felt around the base, then you should insert your index finger, feeling as if it has pierced through; and either uncover or feel between your thumb and the syphilitic ulcer or the char, then cut away what is persistent; since there is no need to struggle if it cannot be healed.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is possible to heal some, but this rarely occurs; and the aid that is made, if it is to heat the subtle cauterizer according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said before; and to insert it all at once into the fistula, until it reaches beyond the base; and do this twice or three times, until you know that these chars have been removed, which are similar to an arrowhead; then the cure of wounds is applied with burdock, until those chars have come out, then the cure of ointment is applied, applying char and sealing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healthy, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not thus healthy, then nothing else can be healthy; and if the tendon attempts to tear, and does not perforate just where it is based, and between your thumb and the tent a thick covering of char or syfac, and you see the fistula at which the covering stops; if the copper begins at the beginning of the fistula, and goes ahead of the tent, and then the cauterization after, until it comes to the top of the tent; and it will be delivered from the tendon, and closed; then wipe off those charred parts that seem like an eagle's quill, and none should remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if you cannot reduce it, and cut between you and the work, then cauterize with fire or medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization assembles two things: to know, the burning of these charred chars, and the stoppage of blood and the scabbing of moisture; then cure tents boiled in butter or in broken chocolate, as long as the wounds gush blood, and is the chars burned in the wound; then cure the wound of sore throats by pouring durable charcoal, and are the medicines dried.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if the fistula comes from just above the base, and is far from the body, then press on the top or base, and examine it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between them is the thread or the skin or charcoal, where it is about to perforate, if there are no other remedies except hope and faith, by the administration of one of the three methods: either you cauterize it as we have said, or you cut it just above the base, or if you can put tents and cure it as we have said; and do not go too far in front, so that you do not cover the foundation that holds the base, and bring the excretions out through the way of volition; then cure it as we have said; perhaps it will be healed, or you remove that covering and clean it as soon as it is cut below the base, or by tent or other instrument appointed; then clean the charred part that is in the wound, as much as you can; then try to restore the wound, and to keep the fistula in the part before the base: if there is a lighter thing to the pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes fistulas are made in this way: and when you push the tent into the fistula, it is where it costs at the base of the skin above the flesh, then take a tent perforated at the head according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And push the thread into the fistula, and push the tent along the entire thread in the fistula until it reaches the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is not successful at the base of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread of that one, so that you push your other or base; and take the head of the thread, and assemble the two pieces together, and hold them against each other, and leave it for a day or two; and do not hold them once, until the thread covers these charcoals that are between the two, and heal; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, then perforate it in all ways that you can, unless it is too much in front.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not suit to place the bandage too much in front, and then treat it as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny spinous bone that is made into the fistula is very sharp and one-sided; on the other hand, not, because we do not know what we should not know, as you see here.
des emorroydes	Des swellings
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Swellings are according to two ways: either they are inside the foundation, like grains of resin, and there are small and large ones, and some have blood, and others have a little bit of urine, or a little bit of blood, and they have the color of the skin; and the treatment of those that are inside the foundation is that you command the patient to sweat so he can move in other rooms, as long as the foundation is not wet, and the child opens; if you hurry, and then pull them out with pincers, or hold them with your nail, then cover their roots; and if the tendons cannot hold them because of their moisture, take them to a cloth, or to a linen cloth, or to a piece of cloth; and stretch them to both sides, then cover them, and powder with some hot powders that are in the cauterizing chapter, or cauterize them as it is said in the chapter of cauterizing, and treat them with other treatments until they are healed; and if the foundation cannot come out, use a dressing made of mustard and aspergillum to clean what is inside the foundation, so that it can come out openly; and if the swellings are painful, and the child is strong from the foundation, then the treatment is light; and it is that you pull them with your nail or pincers, and cover them, then treat them as we have said, until they are healed, and do not fear the incision by iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to suture the wound in this manner: take a thread of twisted wool, and make an awl with it, then draw the thread through the eye of the needle from the other side, and pierce the needle from the other part, and pull the two ends of the thread out of the needle, and if it is too wide; then straighten the thread formally, then untie the thread, and pull out the needle, and do so with all the others, and leave one to let the excess blood out; then put on the bottom of the wound a piece of linen cloth dipped in rose oil or cerus, and put it on the bottom, and command the patient to rest; then let him rest until they are healed, and when they are healed, treat them with ointment and other treatment until they are healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	dryly and firmly at the base
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	often there is dryness at the base of the intestines, and due to constriction of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary to reset the bone at the point of a spatula or at your angle, which does not let it moisten; then cure it as it should be while it is dry; and if it cannot be cured, then begin the razor stronger than before until it is healed, and then it should be scraped; then cure it as it should be while it is healed.
dou fremit	high fever
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Fever is a small appearance that is deformed before the body, and it goes up to the head; and sometimes the fever returns, and one feels as if dead from fever, and it comes throughout the body, and more so in the hands than in other parts.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a quill from a goose pen, or a strong vulture quill, and place that quill on the fever, so that the circles of the fever encircle the fever all around; then turn your hand to the entire quill until you cover the fever all around, and put it in front, and extract the fever from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you see, do this as if it were a thunderbolt or an iron bar of this form, and be subtle in removing and drawing up:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not make a mistake, to hold the point and press it; and if you see, cauterize the heat, as it is in front or the chapter of the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of this form of the clister
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one ever made a clister of silver or copper, or iron melted or sharp; and no one ever made these instruments small and large, according to those with which they were familiar.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, those who are to be treated for children and the weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of this belt is small and large if it is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and there should be a disadvantage where the belly is tied, as you see, and the threads are inside perforated; and on one side there should be II holes, and on the other I; and the belly should have medicines from a beast's bladder or parchment, and it should be perforated all around with small holes, and between each hole there should be one inch of space, then bolt in these holes X or Y threads crisscross, and tie the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, if the thread is to the instrument before one strong thread, then close; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil the head of the poultice with oil or a similar substance, then squeeze it out and apply it to both hands together until all the soreness is gone, then remove the poultice and lift the patient's legs to the side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let it come out as much as possible; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you apply the poultice for a disease of intestinal discharge, and the medicine wants to come out, restart it as long as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the thorn is embedded in the base or in an abscess, it should be removed as delicately as for a child; and this is the form of the delicate removal with the skin being stretched over it:
des plaies	with wounds:
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the treatment of wounds; now we will tell you about the treatment of hands and medicine, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are different according to what they are made of, and according to the places or wounds that are made, and for what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing with a dart, and cutting of spear or dagger, or of lance or staff or arrow, or similar things; or those that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that goes through the neck, or the head, or the foot, or the belly, or the liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds of the head, because its chapter comes first.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or the bone is not broken, take care if it is an insertion of an arrow or similar things, and the skin is completely torn and the wound is large, and you doubt lightly of an abscess: if you do this immediately cleanse the wound itself if there is little blood from the wound, and cleanse the opposite part; and avoid the evils of overeating and heavy foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to cleanse, let him eat light food, and do not drink wine, and do not change his diet; and put on the wound, if an abscess comes, cotton moistened in rose oil alone, or in sterile wine; and if there is no abscess, put on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, powder that I will say a little later; and if the wound has been moved, put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a tailor's awl and similar, and the lips cannot come together by themselves, then sew them together, as I will say in the treatment of belly wounds, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to bone, and can be moved but does not hold but only at a point, then cover it with a bandage; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat soft foods, such as tests and cooked grain, like chickens, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you have leather or purulence that does not touch the bone, then cover it all with the purulence, and pour in strong wine, then treat it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, without cutting, and it cannot be stopped by medicines, then tie the artery, and if you have leather that dislodges, then tie it with a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and you should put in this powder that soothes as soon as the wound has moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; fresh chalk three parts, and the powder finely, and fill the wound, and bandage it tightly, until it heals well and joins all its tissue; then tie it securely, and leave it undisturbed, unless it swells; for one should not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	One should never use chalk alone, when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but only when the wound has moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb has moved the wound, immediately after, do not put any of this powder; but put on some ointments digested, or arrowroot flour made with honey and egg, as long as it is damp; then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a small bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with fine forceps; and I will tell you about the main fractures afterwards.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If a wound comes to the neck and it is simple, there is no difference between this and the main fracture, but if the neck nerves or the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a bone, there is no other method than to let the care, and not put anything restricting, because it hurts bones and makes them recede; and do not put anything sharp on the wound, for the substance of bones is cold, and the continuation of such things is with the brain, which is one of the highest members; but let the medicine be soft, like chalz washed in warm sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and the linen washed in warm sweet water, and other stones of this manner, and gently moist.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with a broad bandage, and treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the bone is shaved and filled with pus, then pierce or below the bone; and if the artery is cut, and blood flows, then remove it, and bandage, and cauterize as appropriate; and if the spine of the neck is cut, or the veins, and the conductor is preserved, by which the flesh goes, if the spine above the neck bone, and do not touch the neck but return it according to its natural shape; then gradually tighten, and leave for some time, then treat the wounds until they are healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then remove it; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove them all if you can, and those that you cannot, leave until the wound heals, and is aligned and cleaned. And if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder that I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if he has bone in the wound and there is a fistula, then treat it as I have described in his chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from arrow or sword
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from arrow or sword, and the wound is deep, look to see if the hairs on the wound are growing ventilated: cut away that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh all over blood, do not put powder in the first hour for the blood that it does not stick together, and return to the heart, and cure the pain; but put attractive ointment, and tie it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, put old cotton in the wound to draw out the moisture, and let it rest for three hours, or four, or more; then there will be no spasm, nor tremor of the heart from elsewhere; and when you see the good dispositions, cut away that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the wounds of tents and other wounds, until they are healed; and if they cannot be healed, and work, then make incisions as there may have been fistulas; thus cure as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from an arrow or sword, and it is simple, or deeper, or at the back, then cure as one should for what is in front; if it is large, stitch; and if it is small, powder, and if it has penetrated into the bone, and has broken pieces, then apply to the wound, and remove the foreign bodies if they are desired; and if they are not desired, let the wound rot, it will lessen the extractions; and for other wounds in other members, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	belly rupture
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the belly is great and common and small; from the great wound, once the intestines or the nerves of the intestines escape, by which the insertion of them occurs; and the wound is more painful, and often the small wound is worse than the large one, because it is easier to put the intestines back in if they are not put back in at once; for the intestines swell quickly when they feel the cold, if they are put back in gently, and because the middle wound is worth more, because it is easier to sew up the intestines to their place as with other wounds.
