And I will say one by one and explain each of the four ways in which the rupture of the belly occurs: the two common costures are in the costure of the belly, and the costure of other wounds of the body, and two other particular costures are common to other wounds; and all the same, they are more particular with the costure of the belly, and I will say one by one and explain each.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the inside is injured, and it is easy to set, then it is done in one of two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is swollen by the heat.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is hot, warm it in this way: moisten a sponge or a handful of dry salt alone, or cook in boiling water and cider vinegar and spike; and heat the intestine until it swells is softened; and never do this restraining, and it is better to let it cool slowly.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling separate, if the intestine is moist or alkaline and the wounds are cooked, for this is aligned with the entry of a little thing; and if it cannot enter, make a small incision in the instrument used to remove tartar; and the first cure is to stop bleeding, which we should not cut without great necessity, and this is the instrument for cutting: if you cut from inside the beak and outside, and cut the shape.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine jumps out, put it back in its natural shape according to its own proper place, if you can, for this is useful.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the part away from the belly, it is necessary that you make the patient lie on their back, and put their legs higher than their head; and if it is in the part away from the belly, put the head and the worst part higher than the other parts, and thus manage as I said for large and medium-sized wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, apply what is appropriate, then put between your hands the painful remedy that covers the entire wound at its hand, and brings together the lips; and this is the common way of stitching, and it is that you hold a needle or several, depending on the quantity of the wound's size, leaving one inch of the wound's head to two, and then insert a needle with good strong thread; and pierce the two skins with the two skin-needles, which are outside the skin from inside, as far as you make the wound pierced from that part, and bring together the two skin-needles four together; then wind the doubled thread around the needle on both sides, and then bring together the wound's edges evenly, leaving one inch, and then insert another needle; and tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this according to what you have with the needles, until the whole wound is closed; and let the needles be medium, between thin and thick, because the thin needles cover the entire skin, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: for this reason they should be medium; and do not put the needles too far from the skin and the flesh, so that they do not cut and open the wound before the sewing; and then cover the edges of the needles, so that they do not bleed the wound at night, and put tents or cloths on the edges of the needles to hold them, and leave them until the wound is sewn; and this way of stitching with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because it requires one needle or two to second stitching, and it is that you bring together the skin-needles and the skin-needles together with a needle that has good strong thread; and when you have pierced these edges all four together, then bend the needle to the part where you started, in the way of sewing, and leave one inch between each stitch; this stitch is the man, and I sewed a wound that someone had in the belly, which was torn by a knife, and the wound was more than one inch wide, and it was out of the intestines by two inches wide, and the wound was inside the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine after it had been out for 24 hours, and the wound was dressed with ointment after 15 hours, and it was treated, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the mother thought he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with any ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine; and I changed the dressing on the wound twice a day with old cotton, and washed it with honey water until he healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	I will now tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle and the thread from the inside of the part in front of it; when it has pierced the curved part on the right, then the head of the suture or the stitch where you inserted the needle, and pierce it again from another part of the inside of the part in front of it; and the understanding of this sewing is that you sew as the furriers make the furs, and leave one end of the suture once, and then take it from another part, until the sewing is all completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galen properly calls, is such that anyone can do, who assembles the two parts together naturally, and applies one of the main needles to the other head, in a similar way: stick an needle or main needle close to the part to be sewn, and make it pierce only that part alone, and leave the two needles of the syfac; then turn the needle, and make it pierce from the front part downwards through the middle, the two needles of the syfac; then pierce both from the front part downwards through the middle, in two other needles that are on the other side; and this is the easiest method of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	For those who say this, and no one testifies to it, that the stomach should be sewn with two needles, or one in each; and one should be put on one side, and the other on the other, in the manner of those who embroider corroies; and sutures that when the tear is in the stomach, it is more painful than other stitches of the stomach.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you cut the fresh wound to all its blood, provided the doctor has moved it, then put back the intestine, and the cloth; then put on powder mixed with charcoal, and if the doctor has moved it, then put on any ointment that is present, until the wound closes; and bind the bandage, and sound the sifac, and the mirach; then treat the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicines, then as soon as it begins to bleed, cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other medical treatment in many positions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound does not make communication with principal members, then it is necessary to apply a light oil of temperate warmth, or rose oil, and place it around the wounds, and separate the bones; and if it feels pain or putrefaction in the belly, and often happens, then clysterize with black wine, and immediately if the putrefaction comes to the intestines; and perforate within, and scrape what is inside, the large intestines being lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine called "jeun" cannot heal when it is raw, because of the thinness of its veins that are in it, and due to the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity to nerve nature.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the gut jumps out of the wound, put it back in as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned black, you must tie the part that is black, for blood vessels do not come into it, because it has veins and arteries; then cover what is between the limb, and hang the two ends down from the side of the wound towards the back to straighten the extraction when the gut falls, and the wound closes.
de la routure dou boueil	of the tearing of boiled bread
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is rent, and the wound is small, if it can be restored to some men, for I saw that one man was pierced through the belly by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became an ulcer, and in it were excretions and foulness; I put care according to what I knew, and did not cease to carefully treat it until it was healed, and the men recovered.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw it being sewn up, I doubted that the hairs were not in his intestine; and there was no harm, but he remained in better conditions, and eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when one has a small wound in the intestine, one should be bound in such a way: take a large needle, then gather the lips of the wound, and when the needle is over the mouth, so it holds the mouth above; then cover the test with the other needle, and hold it so that it cannot slip, then put the other needle again in that way until the wound is completely closed.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the shoulder joint catches fire inside, and no harm comes to the patient, and it can be tied with a thin thread that is taken from the intestine of an animal, in such a way: take the end of this intestine thread that is very dirty, and then tie it to the end of this thin silk thread, then pull the thread through the needle, and sew the intestine, and roll it into the wound; and this method of sewing is no more than according to the way of faith and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the intestines, there is no skill or health, only thinness.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of a fistula or that she is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	that every wound or abscess, when it is covered over, is universally called "fistula", and specifically when it is cut open and healed.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to its hardness and whiteness, where no pain is felt, and it is cut open like the quill of an eye; and sometimes it is clear and sometimes deep; sometimes small and sometimes enough; and I have spoken about it in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no char, except by one of the EIGHT causes: namely, by the smallness of the blood or flesh; or by its evil nature; or because there is a hard char inside and on the lips, which does not allow new char to grow; or there is too much blood; or the wounds are poor, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is like pestilence; or because the property in the region is late in digestion, and late in health, and flows by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary for me to tell you about the treatment of fistulas that is done by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come to large veins, and to arteries, and to nerves, or to the face, or to the intestine, or to the bladder, or to any of the costal bones, or to the spine of the back, or to any joint of the hands or feet; and if they come to the property of the principal member, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All fistulas of this kind are a difficult cure, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the joint that I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you know how to treat it, take a tin or iron needle, if the fistula is straight, if the quill; and if the fistula is crooked, take a thin tin of plunger, because the plungers penetrate around the crookedness; and if the fistula has many holes and you cannot well sew it by tents, then cauterize one of the holes, for the moisture goes from one hole to another, and cleanses it; then treat it carefully to your power, that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and if it is cut in front, and ask the patient well about the pain he feels when you press with your hand, and where he feels it; and when you will know truly where it is, and whether it is far from joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, if it is according to what I have told you, and remove the cause and the rotten parts that are inside; and then treat it until it is healed, and if the fistula is deeply placed in the right place, then cut it open as much as you can, then put soft tents of medicine, and push them up to the head of the fistule, until the medicine corrodes the superfluity that remains at the bottom; and then put clean ointment on a clean cloth, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is rotten from the fistule, then cut.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves do not cause you pain or harm your main limbs, as we have said; and if the tooth is exposed, and there is corruption and blackness, then clean the corruption until it is completely removed, then treat the things inside as much as possible until they are healed; and if they are not healed, and remain as before, then you must remove them as before: if it exposes and wants to come out as much as possible, and remove all the corruption, then restore the tooth; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, then it is too deeply rooted, and you cannot reach it; if there is no other means than patience; and if there is a small rotten bone, and you can pull it out with pliers, then extract it with the suitable tool, and if there are many bones, then remove them all, and do not leave any behind; and if the moisture makes it against you, and there is no error or fear, then use heat and moisture and char, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you cannot remove them within an hour, apply something soothing to the wound, and leave it until the bone is surrounded by flesh, and then they will be more easily broken; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, raise the corruption as far as the bone is not entirely ossified, then reopen the wound; and if there is a great part of the corruption coming from the bone; if it should be covered and covered with what comes from the bone, and then treat it until it is sound; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The young man was around 30 years old, who had pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the chest, so that the matters came to the leg, and he was inflamed by a large abscess, and there was no cause to open; but the doctor opened it too high, and they drained a lot of matter, and it became a fistula, and many people were sick with the body and moisture from the chest; and many doctors treated him within two years, and there was no healing in the art of hands, until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines that they used to treat it, and what was going through the pores to the great chest; and his chest became red like a lemon.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of these gaps, and then I searched all the gaps, and found that one was coming towards the other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then stayed there, and took out in one of the gaps until I discovered a part of the bone, and found it rotten and perforated, and the corruption was coming to the bone from inside; I saw that the rotten bone appeared to me, and I thought that there was no other corruption except what I had seen; and I began to treat the wound with various medicines for a long time, but could not heal it; then I started again, and discovered the bone as before, and found the continuous corruption in the bone, and saw it, and then I took it out, and I felt pain in the limb; but I could not take it all out, so I took around a palm of the bone, and treated it completely, then I put medicines back on; it became healthy and healed quickly, but it did not want to start again except for the weakness of the pain, which could not bear, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For the evacuation of blood often occurred, but he was completely cured, and in place of the bone grew a hard cartilage, and it was of good disposition and had no harm or contrary effect throughout, neither at first nor later.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, it should be done in this way: take a thin linen cloth, and stretch it at the head of the bone that opens, and command that it not extend upwards; and put another thicker linen strip above the first one, and tie it over the cartilage that is on top of the bone, and stretch the head, so that you can remove the corrupted cartilage from outside, and reveal the cartilage over the part where you want to be, that it does not stick to the cartilage; and put a poultice or a cloth of something else beside the bone to cover the corrupted cartilage; and it should be done so that one can see and feel the corruption, and it should be done again another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the tooth is rotted, and not opened, and the rot is in the middle or in one part, then remove the entire tooth; then put the thread on the other side of the corruption, and sew from one part to the other the corruption, and let the thread be as long as possible, as we have said; and if the rot is in the joint, then copper the corrupted joint, and sew the bone or what it contains from the other side; and if the rot is in the continuation of the two joints, then there is no other way than to cover it; and if the rot is at the fingertip, or at the tip of the toe, then this thing is very difficult, but nevertheless you should inquire about this corrosion, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but do not let the vein or nerve do the opposite; and know that the tools for covering these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of teeth, and their size and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and therefore you should prepare a tool for each similar work of craftsmanship; and know that the work will show you the tool that you will have to use, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so consider the tool that you have according to what it should be.
dou feu	for the fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints will become deformed or due to the lack of, or due to the absence; and when you have medicine for that corrosion by the cure of medicines, and it does not help, then you must cover that member up to the joint where the corrosion comes from, so that the pain escapes by the means of death, or by malice, which is greater, due to the lack of the member; and the signs are that the members become black, so that it seems as if it were burned by fire, and afterwards becomes darker, then those corrosions of member after member take hold of the whole body; if you hurry to cover, and if it is due to the sting of some poisonous animals, such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and similar, if the corrosion is at the head of the joint, then cover it, and do not give them any space to come to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes out of the hand, if the cope is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come out to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, if the cope at the shoulder; and if it passes the shoulder, it is death, and there is no other remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and thus do all as the corrosion comes or pierces: if it comes in the first joint, if the cope after the other joint; and if it comes to the pierce, if the cope all the pierce; and if it goes up the leg, if the cope at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other means than that the limb is dead; and the way of the copper or the cloth to bandage the member is that you tie it above and below, and place some bandages on one side, and others on the other side, and cut the flesh between the two sides at a span wide, until the bone is exposed; then the copper or cloth, and put some linen from each part so that the wound does not touch the healthy skin, and comes to the other injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood flows when you are working and cutting, cauterize the wound quickly with a hot iron, or apply some powders that stop bleeding; then continue your treatment until it is completed, then bind the injured limb with a bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his foot: he had a black spot that seemed like burning by fire, and that corrosion first appeared on his sole of the foot, taking over the whole foot; and when the doctor saw the corrosion, he covered the foot, and it was healed; but after a long time, the corrosion appeared again on the second toe, and it came to me, and I applied some repercussive things after washing the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he thought that I would cut off his toe, and he did not want, because he had no hope of being cured; and he despaird completely, and returned to his land, and covered his toe, and it was healed; and I have not told you anything else except for the reason why others do this, if they have a need.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes abscess in the joint, and it stays so long that it causes great swelling; then they burst and pierce, and in their bursting, the skin remains like a bag; and the skin above is also as thin as cloth, and does not stick to the bone, nor to the nerve, and such diseases are called "sinus", and are not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it reaches the bone from both sides, it is called "fistula"; and the skin is that you cover that skin all around, and especially when it is thin, like cloth; and does not rot for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have sworn that the skin has hardened, and corruption is not yet present, and the skin is charred, then the following cure should be used: check if the breasts are large, and the nipples have a foul odor, then use an Egyptian plaster made as follows: take equal amounts of aloe, oil, and licorice, cook them together in a small vessel over the fire until the medicine turns red and thickens like honey; then apply it to the breasts, bandage them tightly, and leave it for two hours, then remove it by sprinkling; do this many times until the breasts are clean and soft; and if the patient cannot bear the pain or the Egyptian plaster and water made of ashes do not help, then use a plaster of honey and wine with a little licorice powder; or use a plaster of honey and melted wine, which has the property of cleaning and washing, and the wine makes the flesh sore; and when you have done this, and you are sure that the breasts are clean, then apply a definitive plaster made with rose oil and wine; or use some medicines and ointments, as I have mentioned their properties for treating wounds; and if the nipple is too small, and the plaster cannot enter, then enlarge it with a small iron, and put in a tent of Egyptian ointment or basilicon, until it is large enough to enter; and if the wound is too large, then cover it with a cloth or bandage where the plaster or the breast can enter, and if the nipple that is above is too high, then place it below where it can enter.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement. Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if his breast becomes swollen and undigested after many hours, tear that the breast does not become misshapen.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons are cut after long tension, do not despair of health, for health approaches.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.
