Those with excessive superfluities rise from old wine, or vinegar of sugar, or decoction of anise or chamomile, or other similar things; and they should not be purged before the bath, but after the bath for one hour or two; and they should not sleep after the enema, and it is good that they move, when they should be enemized and when they are enemized.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And if those who are purged are choleric, and they are not too agitated and inflamed; then it is good that they take cold things, such as green apples and endives and leeks at the spoon, and similar things; and thin gruel, and cataplasm of St. John's wort, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold constitution, take honey syrup, aromatic wine between old and new, and a little mustard, and small olives and pigeons; and the day they are to vomit, they should drink more than they eat; and it is necessary to give some men triphala or muscat before vomiting, or after, to strengthen the main members; and the subtle ones should not drink it, but only those who are strong.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are applied to the body are those that are applied to the liver, and to the spleen, and to the sciatica, and to the stomach and the belly and the ribs, because these members do not suffer from being applied on the outside, and no one does it except to draw blood from member to member, as we put suction cups on the breasts when the baby is born; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we apply suction cups to the stomach and to the belly to ease the member; and remove the pain, when there is an abscess or a stone, if it is removed by its attractive power perhaps the abscess, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it is done as soon as they put it on the liver and on the spleen when there is retained viscosity, and these suction cups are administered empty for moisture only; and sometimes they are administered together with heat, and sometimes with cold water, such as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way one fills the suction cup with hot boiling water, or with cold water where there are harmful herbs cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction device administered by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has two inches of width and half a palm of depth, and it has or is covered with a small hole in the middle, as to put a needle, and it is made of tin, so that it does not burn the skin when placed on the limb; and it has in the middle a thin rod of tin or iron, for placing a candle, and they are large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them; for the suction devices of children are different from those of the elderly, and the thin ones are different from the thick ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And one should thus place this suction cup on the limb: take the wax or liniment, and put it inside the suction cup through the rod that is inside the suction cup, so that the light may be at the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the hair; then put it on the limb, and you must do so as we have said, so that when one wants, if the vapor comes out, and remove the suction cup; and take the liniment as before, and repeat often, if you have the skill.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction cup that is administered in the disease of pleurisy, at all times, there is no rod or stopper, and it is not administered until it is full of water, and it is placed on the limb alone; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Sansues are not used except in members where one cannot place suction for their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar things; and in similar members, such as fingers or toes, and others like them; and the quality of using sansues is that when you remove sansues that are in soft waters without pressure, take them; and put them in soft water until they are familiar, and have nothing in their bellies; and then cleanse the member with blood and suction, then rub the member until it is red, and put on the sansues; and when they are plain and blackened, if it is a place where one can place suction, place it, for this is very helpful.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, first raise the limb from the lowest to the highest position, well, and then wipe it; if the wound is too large after the fur of the fleas, then dip a piece of linen in cold water, and place it on top, until the wound is cleansed; and if the wound multiplies, then place on top vitriol shattered, or galls, and similar things, until it is cleansed; or you place half of pounded beans on the wound, and leave them until they dry on the limb, it will stop now; and if you have more, take other fleas.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the snakes do not want to take, rub the wound with fresh blood, or you have a needle as long as the snake, and then place them on top, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will bite; and when you see that they are biting, powder with a little aloe and beaten silk, or ash, so they will now die.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it restores fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Listen, dear son, that the foolish people may not see this chapter, that they have never seen any of the ancient books, nor have read any letters; and for this reason the science is hidden in our land, because I found none good; and I know nothing, except by the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experiment, and by the custom of my life; and I have described to you in this chapter what is contained, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have shown clearly the forms of the instruments that are necessary, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say or prologue of this book the sums of the word and the chapters where the wise put his understanding, and stay on the truth, so that those who are experienced find and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when fracture or dislocation or twisting or wounding comes to anyone, it is necessary to treat the injury on one side and the other, if nothing stops you, as weakness of body, or children, or elderly; or if the pain is not very great, or too cold; and use cold remedies, that is to say, cold jackets, and eagle and chicken broth, and do not drink wine, and do not use any fatty broths, and do not fill oneself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have no doubt of abscess, or spreading of matter to the member; then the injuries return to their usual government as they have used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to apply a poultice of meat that causes large swelling, or has viscosity, such as cooked wheat, and rice, and tests, and peas, and pancakes of milk, and eggs, and fish, and fresh wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the poultice causes pain and heals more quickly than the break.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the elderly and infirm do not heal well or mend according to their nature due to the weakness of the limbs, nor those who are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but rather, reset and joint the member together, as it was before, until it is strong again; and do not let them work at all, and for this reason, it is necessary to apply a poultice of large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And the fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the hand or leg, and I will tell you all the ways of fracture in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes through the bone, and another in soaking, like the tip of a quill for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a small cut.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each kind has its own method, and its proper instrument in restoration, according to what memory comes to its mind; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the leg is twisted, and open wide by deficiency, and it is pressed by the hand; and when there is no tortuosity or it is not at the touch, and the pains are not great, if there is no fracture; but it can well have tortuosity, or a cut, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	It is not necessary that you move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after this, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And if the fracture that was in arvoil is now separated into two parts, you should now put them back together evenly, as with abscesses that come and go; and if they are hard and painful, do not let any joint move until the abscess is soothed; then gently put them back to where you can lightly and safely, and if the restoration of this is lighter than the restorations of those who have pieces, then constrain it as it should be after this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if it is broken into pieces in the bone, if it is a hand or foot, or to your hand if it is small members, or to two strings, or to one string and to your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are joined, you should join them with all your skill to avoid causing further injury or pain; and properly set the two bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not quite right: if it is well dressed, and do not strain it too much, or press it as those who bring their work by force and contraction to the member, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a point, carefully keep it from moving the painful part, neither while awake nor while sleeping, nor while turning, nor in any other way; and make sure that the limb is so secure that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, it is not yet at a point, and it should be put in the best position so that it feels no pain; and make sure it is placed straight, so that twisting does not come when it is restored; and the quality of the limb broken depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The qualities of the limb broken depend on their size, greatness, and form.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, such as arms and legs and similar ones: if it is necessary to wrap them in soft and thin linen cloths; and those that are large, such as thighs: if it is necessary to wrap them in a wide and strong cloth, because the wide bands embrace the whole member, and hold it evenly from all parts, so that there is no gap; then wrap light bandages around the limb, three or four times according to the length of the limb, and hold your hand a little on every part of the cloth, then go above the fracture and hold it less, than the fracture can be moved a little; then soften the cloth a little and a little, until you grasp a large part of the healthy flesh, then take another cloth and return around the broken part; then return to the part away from the fracture, and hold it evenly, not too hard or too forcefully, as we have said in the first chapter above; then place between the cloths linen or cloth bandages, until they are all even, then tie everything together from above with a bandage, and then put your well-made bandages on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or boil, put something soothing on the abscess to open it, and what opens the abscess, and leave it like that for some time; then strain it through a cloth, and be of half a wide bowl cleanly, or of wood from which the lancets are made, or of palm leaves, and be according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But the thread that one puts on the wound should be a little larger and wider than the others; and it should also be as long as the member of smallness or greatness requires; then strain it through the threads just as you did in the first layer, then tie it under a thread evenly, as in the first layer over the break; the tighter it is, the less; and it should be that the threads are medium, neither too thick nor too thin, and of linen; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen works of the foliage that make their strings of linen twisted, and it is great error, because the bandage cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not be that there is less than two fingers' space between each thread.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the wounds are closed by the pricks of the needles after straightening them in their proper place, put some unbleached linen or cotton between them so that they do not become infected.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bone broken, and the splint is broken, I will tell you the treatment after this.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And do not strain with needles all the broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not good to put needles immediately after 5 or 7 days, or more depending on your risk of abscess; and get the manner of ancient plasters to restore breakage, dislocation, and torsion: and it is that you take some flour that is kept as a wall of the mill, and mix it with much water, and put this mixture, not too clear nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common method of the plaster restoring breakage to many positions, and especially for women and small children, for it is not too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of healing fractures, dislocations, and twists: take alabaster and lavender and enule and asafetida and Arabic gum and myrrh, each 1 Z.; mire and aloes, each 5 Z.; alechil 8 Z.; and grind them into a powder, and mix with honey; if the patient's constitution is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it quickly heals broken bones, and it saves many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of healing twists: take myrrh and valerian, each 10 Z.; mire and aloes, each 8 Z.; acacia 6 Z.; bolic armenic 10 Z., and grind them well, and mix with vinegar or honey, and administer.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another way to treat joints and bones that are dislocated from their place, and to ease the pain, and to use the bone and the broken piece: take a new bone, and soften it in oil and cooked fat, and put it on the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal completely, but it is good for easing out abscesses, and properly treats the pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to treat broken bones that heal: take dried fig leaves and earthworms, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to treat the healing of broken bones and to ease the remaining pain from the abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of viscum, chamomile, flowers of violets, flour of each one in equal parts; and grind, and mix with wine, and if the limbs are cold, mix with mustard mixed with water, or dry mustard, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to apply, besides the first, when an abscess is difficult to restore to the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the root of viscum, and seeds of linseed, balm, melissa, and sansuce, and flowers of violets and chamomile, of all one part; and grind, and mix with mustard mixed with salt, or dry mustard, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hippocrates said in his book that one should not put on a broken limb to restore it, except for a mixture of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he said that it should be between two, neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen said that one should put on a broken limb to restore it, with dry things slightly warm, such as mercury and aloes and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to treat the injury and pain: take mugwort and horsehair, or feathers of an owl, and smash them, and mix them equally, and make a plaster and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then release the joint a little later, and be careful if there is no pain or the bone of its limb moves; do not release it by force again. And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, without rest or swelling, then hasten, and release it, and remove the plaster now; and take a light bandage, and moist sponge from sea water, and soak in hot, and raise the limb, until the itching stops, and calm the pain; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, moistened in hot or rose oil, and tie with a nut, until you are sure of no abscess forming; and relieve the inflammation of the limb, and be calmed the pain, then continue the thin bandage, and a little plaster, and do not strain it as much as before; gradually until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess is red and swollen and painful and inflamed, and you have the skill of plastering and bandaging, then if it starts to recur, do so evenly as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if it does not come to the limb at all as we have said, then wait for three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, as long as the bone is not healed, and approach the joint from above; then restrain it more than before, and increase its flesh, as I have said before; and if you see that the bone is healed more than necessary, then do not let any new pus come to it; then apply hot water frequently when you remove it, every day, and loosen the bandage a little; by this method, then cut off the pus from the limb, and repair hastily what the foolish ones do, which tortures the member: it is bad, and if it is not done properly, I see nothing but the loss and doing it straight.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various methods of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of breaking are, and various shapes, and the causes are distinguished; for there are breaks that are made by the percussion of a spear, and the collarbone completely breaks the bone at its face which is outside the bone, as it does hatchet or fust; and because of this method of breakage is called «haichure».
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	Or the spear pierces the bone from above through the side, and this method of breakage is called «absolute»; and it is the wound of these two breaks great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is percussion embedded, or cutting from the side of a spear, or to fall on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has a fracture that is persistent, which approaches the thread that is outside of the bone, or it is above the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is healed into the bone as thin as a hair, and it is the fracture called "hair-like"; and if the wound made by piercing with an arrow, or falling, or similar thing, and makes the piece of the bone enter below, and is like the nails when they are driven through the chimneys; then the arrow enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And it happens more often in those who have or a moist head bone, such as the head of a child; and they have all these kinds of fractures where small pieces are removed like these; and I will speak about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all ways of breaking them by pulling up on them, and inquiry with probes, and by the rotten wood that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known because when the bone is exposed and rubbed against it, the black breakage becomes apparent.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the breakage, be careful of the bad accident, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, and loss of consciousness, and extension, and paleness, and fever ague, and the eyes issuing forth and reddening, and other similar things in many conditions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any obvious injury, and you hope for recovery, begin treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the broken bone comes first to you, and it is in the thigh, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the injury as you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the lower part, then you must remove the bone before the seventh day, provided that the skin over the bone is not corrupted, and the accidents that we have mentioned occur.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the broken bone comes close to the skin that covers the brain, then it is necessary to cut away the damaged part in this way: and you should grasp the head of the painful wound, and uncover the bone in all ways that you can, and over the shape of the wound more softly than you can, and if blood comes out when the bone is exposed, or an abscess forms, help it according to what is necessary, and it is necessary to fill the wound with moistened linen cloths in rose oil; and let the wound rest until the abscess is relieved, and make sure that blood does not come out; then begin around the bone to remove, and this is done according to the two methods of work: one method is that you cut tightly against the edge in front, and this is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And in the second manner, you should have many different cuts, some narrow and some wide, and sharp and made of iron inde; and work lightly, so as not to wound the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the tooth is very hard and out of place, it is necessary that you perforate around it, as long as you administer cuts with tarriers, not piercing through the tooth beyond the test, and it should have above the point a margin or circle, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the tooth; and you should have many of these, so that each comes in its own place of the spine of the tooth, so that you have tarriers for all teeth; and this is the form of the three ways of tarriers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	To pierce through the broken bone, you should place the tip of your tool on top of the bone and turn it back to your right until you feel that the bone is pierced; then remove the tool from one side slightly, and do the same around the entire bone, then carefully cut away the space between the bones with a sharp instrument, as subtly and lightly as possible, until you remove the bone to your hand or to any of the tools you have such as forceps or pliers; and be careful not to touch the brain or sinuses.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and removed the bone, it is advisable to remove any remaining fragments of small bones or scales from it with a sharp instrument similar to an incisor, but it should be more delicate and subtle than the other incisor; then treat the wound with tents and ointments as we have mentioned.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of work is that which the Greeks call, which is much safer; and it is very effective, and that is their word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is first necessary that you uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you can insert the lens-shaped piece of this incisive tool, which has this shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one part, and it is the part that is in two pieces, so that the cutter is towards the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so that you lightly cut the bone all around, and be careful of the thread that is outside; if it is near the bone, then lightly cut the bone, because it is cut well without harming, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone's fracture does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only broken from above, and there are small pieces, it is necessary to smooth that roughness, and remove scales with the fine file you should have various quantities of, to manage each limb in the most convenient way, according to the work and the figure of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use coarse files first, and then more fine ones, and do not stop doing this until it is well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hairdressing and fine fracture, it is necessary that you manage according to its direction; and this is a thing that is not returned to the one who put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, it is necessary to apply a cloth of linen, according to the quantity of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth doubled in two or three, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do this more gently than you can, so as not to irritate the wound, then administer by above another remedy, and do not strain it more than to make the wound alone tinge; and leave it thus for a day or two, until the abscess is calmed, then remove it, and administer medicines such as lily roots, flour of vetch, powder of frankincense, and aristolochia, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and place on the wound, and administer liquid medicines without bitterness; and keep the wound clean, so that you do not leave any ointment, or any bandage, for when bandages gather together on the brain, it corrodes and rots, and causes great harm; for when something sharp is placed on the wound, it does not heal.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If no accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, then it is uncertain with doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if no other harm comes except for what medicine has been placed on, that it may have virtue, then you must apply a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and a cloth, and place it on the wound; then cure it with methods of curing as it is necessary, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Never break the two bones above, or one by itself, for they are two bones; and that one is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you break your small finger or thumb, and place the broken part inside your index finger, and in the palm by default, until the bone regrows according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, and guard that the pain does not increase due to your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the upper part of the bone, and cannot reach your finger, it is necessary that you place it on the head of a pin or slightly thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in both parts, make another and hurry to restore the first joint, if you can; otherwise, after the seventh or eighth day, when the wound heals, then place the head of your finger on the palm of your hand with pieces of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Where you break it, there the fracture is; and if the tents are too large, they fill the nostrils.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer how to mill the tents in fire, and die each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think this is good, but it should be milled in the form of an ointment with egg yolk and powdered milk; then leave the tent until the bone is strong and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never once penned in the nostrils with goose feathers, and if the swelling is around, and hold the fracture, and blow the pain away; now do what you see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come to the nose while you are working, put a piece of cloth or cotton wool soaked in rose oil or a small amount of iodine.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If abscesses do not come to the nose, then apply a poultice of mustard flour and powdered incense, mixed with an egg yolk, then place light bandages on it, and do not tie too tightly around the nose; if the broken part of the nose is small and in many pieces, use suitable instruments to fix it, then cut the wound, and treat the injured parts as appropriate, and apply suitable ointments and poultices as needed; and if there is no wound inside the nose, then treat with tents and apply warm compresses until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the jawbone fracture
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured, and there is no wound elsewhere, and the fracture is only so much, and is not broken into two pieces, but rather is crushed inwardly, if one knows it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the fracture is in the right part, you should push your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left jawbone, push your index finger with your right hand, and push the fracture inwardly lightly, and push it to the other hand by default, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is in two, then it is necessary to administer extension of two parts until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if movements of the teeth occur, or a break, then strain them with a gold, silver, or silk thread, and place over the broken jaw, and place over the cloth a double layer; and place over the cloth a great well-made sponge, or a piece of leather evenly long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it with a string so that you can, and command to not move, and feed light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the shape changes, then remove it from the animal, and then put back what was changed; and place a poultice on it, of the flour of the mill with abundant urine or flour of mustard, after you have removed the cerote; and place over the poultice another light cloth, and if the poultice becomes hard, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healed; often it is healed in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	If abscesses come up, then follow what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, do not remove any piece of the bone that is osseous; rather, carefully remove it with unsuitable instruments to this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then enlarge it according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there is none left, then clean the wound, if it is wide, and put on unsuitable bandages to this purpose, to stop bleeding until they are healed.
de la forcele	of the elbow
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The elbow breaks many times in front and behind the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: either it is broken and dislocated into two, and there are pieces, and it is the least heavy to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And if the work is about the break with a wound, you should have two assistants, so that one tends to the injury where the elbow is broken; and the other extends the arm towards the affected part; then set the break evenly to your two hands, so that it forms as it should be, and there is no appearance or movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have the skill to extend further, place a rounded ball of cloth or linen, and as large as your need; extend and relieve the tension, and hold the sphere in your hand, so that you can align the fracture as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder back, because it comes out front, then you should align the fracture as well as possible above its natural position, and place a median ear under the shoulder, and lift the bone of the shoulder until the bone is elevated.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then apply the bandage to your wounds, and if you have loose teeth, it is necessary that you cut through; and carefully suture the pieces, and if the bone cannot be joined for any reason, then use one of the instruments you have; but do not put force on the forceps, to avoid damaging the gums:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it seems like a spoon, and is not too tight, and should be as wide as needed, according to the size of the bone and the skill of the work; and have two prongs, one wide and the other narrow, as the tear in the wound that you made when you sutured the bones; and when you are sure there is no abscess, then clean the wound, and if the tear is small, or you doubt there is an abscess, then use dressings and tents according to the size of the wound.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if an abscess comes, if it bursts, soak the cloth in rose oil and in vinegar and in wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The splinting of the bone, when it is painful and when it is fractured, is that you put it on top of the bone the plaster of the mill powder and some mud, and put it on. Then take a very large bandage of a palm wide, then put the cloth double over the light dressing, and the plaster; then take a subtle staff of three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is hanging down; and put the staff on the fracture, and turn the bandage over the neck, and outside the fracture sane, and outside the fracture painful; and tie each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture evenly, and you see clearly that the staff does not move over the broken bone, reward it every day, and when the bones are healed, hold it; then make the painful part lie on his back, and put what little mud is outside the fracture to raise the fracture in the top; if it aligns the shoulder by the alignment of the space, or you tie the arm to the neck, and if no bad accidents happen, for 20 days; then recommend the plaster, if you see that it has a job, and hold it and let it be so, until it is restored; and it is restored in the most 28 days, and less to some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It rarely happens that the shoulder is broken or out of its place, and it is not fixed except by touch; if the fracture follows the figure of the break, and the bone is placed according to its natural form, in all ways you can; then put powder from the mill with abundance of honey on the limb, and lightly stop it, and put a double cloth on top; then put on a wide and delicate splint, a little wider than the shoulder, and if the splint does not touch any part of the shoulder, then use a piece of linen to make it even; and then tightly bandage all around, so that the splint does not move from its place, and watch the limb every day; and every time it is broken, tighten the bandage, and if the splint is out of place, and cover the wounds on its side; and the shoulder is restored in 20 days or 25 days, And when these numbers are completed, remove it, and be careful, for it is not bones that can be fixed firmly.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone is torn off before the wound heals, and not removed, then cutting into it, and the bone, and do what we have said in the breaking of the malleolus to alleviate an abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	of the breaking of the pis
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The pis is never broken in the middle, but it does happen sometimes; but it breaks often at the back.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines towards the outside, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of movement, and all, and possibly vomits blood, and the bones are open in the broken bone, and the patient does not feel well.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the hairs are carefully arranged over their back, and the hand is placed between the shoulder blades, then the shoulders are pressed, and the ribs of the two sides are held in your hands, and subtly put even to all the ways you can, until the shape of the bone is as it should be; then place bandages and soft ones above the thin bone of salt, or other light one, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and return the limb gently to the back, and gradually strap it, and rewrap it every hour, and if it moves, strap it again; and if it is necessary to remove it for corrosion or itching that comes to the skin, or pain or abscess, then hurry, remove it, and wash the bandage, and apply what has come from methods of healing; then rewrap the bandage, and strap it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	The rib fractures only come from great blows to the chest after the back, and at the neck, and they do not break unless because they are sharp; and the pain is felt well in the interrogation of them.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the plaster, and the bandage of a splint, if you know how to do it.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is inclined inward, it causes great pain and tenderness, as if of pleurisy, because the ribs do not protect; and there is a great deal of blood, and a great deal of blood flow, and this is a great sickness, and the ancients have put much effort into it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And for those who say it is necessary to administer foods that cause the stomach to swell, in order to push the rib out of place.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this unless an abscess is present.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it is present, then lance it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that none of those who put suction cups on the limb for draining are wrong, and this is reasonable; however, doubt arises because the suction cup may not draw out the excess from the limb due to its weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that none of those who cover the limb with linen soaked in olive oil and place tents between the ribs to equalize the fluid around it are wrong, then treat the wound with poultice, food, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the pain is great and the patient cannot bear it due to the bone that does not pierce the skin, and there is doubt, then you must cut above the broken rib on the side, and place a splint on the wound; then you must break the bone, gently pull it out, and then suture the two lips of the wound, if it is large, and treat them with ointments until they are healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes out, place moist cloths on top of the abscess; and treat it while the wound is healing, and let it lie flat on top of the side where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the broken neckbone
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when the breaker of the neckbones appears, and it is rare that they bleed; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if they will be healed or not, if you see their hands softened and swollen and dead, and they cannot move or extend them, and when you touch them with a needle, they do not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	It is known that it is deadly in many positions, and if they move and feel well when you hold them and do not, then know that the joint of the bone is saved, and the pains are healed, if they are treated.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar thing comes to the spine of the back, and you know whether it is healthy or not, if you take notice of whether the feet are soft, and if the accidents that are in their hands, and above the back, there is a sense of ventosities and egestion without volition; and when they lie on their belly, there is egestion without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when they are lying on their back and they want to sit up, they cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	It is a fatal condition: do not labor in its care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to them, it is the lighter condition.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you reward if there is an abscess open, put oil of roses or hen's fat on it until it is soothed; then put on one of the healing plasters and drying, and tie with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that part where you feel the pain, until it is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dry, it is necessary to cover it with a cloth; then take the bone, then gather the two edges of the wound, if it is large, to a seam, then treat the wound with ointment applying charcoal, until it is healed; and if the bone is broken, which is called the "bone of the cow", if you have a pouch in your right hand, put it even on the other hand to your power, then put the plaster and the bandage on top, if you know how; then strain it, and if there is dry bone, do it again, and take the bone, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the ribs of the back
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It rarely happens that the ribs of the back are broken, and if it does, it is not often accompanied by a slight decrease in the chest; making it long, and declining to the side, and coming to the painful joint, and swelling, and inflammation as it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is such that you extend your hand over it, until you are over the broken rib; and cleanse those that are the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is only at the top, then set it evenly until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long or declines to the inside, place the injured limb on its belly until the healing of this fracture is complete.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have placed it evenly, apply the poultice, then place a splint of wood or cloth, and hold the fracture so it does not move; and fill the wound on both sides, until it is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on their uninjured side or on their back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if an abscess forms, do not touch it until the abscess is calmed, and follow what we have previously said; then return to healing, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad accident; and this is how it is done.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The shoulder is the area between the neck and the top of the shoulder. If it is broken, one should restore it according to one of the two methods: one method is that you take a smooth bone, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two broken pieces together and lift them up, and saw the painful part above the seat; then pour some water over the broken arm, as much as it can bear, and put a splint on it, then place any heavy object or the minister extends it below; then put the splint in the patient's hands together, until the broken piece returns as it should be.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other way is that one should press the pain above its shoulder, and hold the hand on its neck, then command the two ministers that one ties what is above the broken bone to his hands, and the other ties behind all of it, and stretches each to its part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	If you see that the extraction is too far, then hold the tie outside of the broken bone, above the broken bone, and stretch each of the ministers to its part.
