Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the broken bone is near the top of the shoulder, then it is necessary to place the tie outside of the shoulder blade, and the other towards the back, outside of the broken bone; and similarly if the broken bone is towards the back, then it is necessary to place the tie gently, without labor, until the broken bone is even with the shoulder, and with the back, then set the fracture as it should be, and stretch it, if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes, do not hold it for more than seven days, and put a poultice of wheat flour and rose oil on it until the abscess is soothed; then hold it, and the manner of holding it is that you place the plaster on the swollen part, then bring the arm up to the shoulder or to the chest; and put a bandage, and hold it on the shoulder or on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, as long as nothing prevents it from moving or the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone does not move, use splints, and put a wider and stronger splint on the break than the others, and have between each splint two inches of space, and each splint should be so large that it passes the break three inches from each side; then hold them, as I said at the beginning of the chapter, more tightly and less distant.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the arrows, and the pressure, as we have said, in the bone where you restore the broken member, and you doubt the abscess is deep, let it lie for seven days, as we have said; then look at the joint every three days, that pruritus does not come to it, or the pus does not come to the limb because it is too tense.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the wound, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents come, but only after three days or more, and the pain lies on its back, and has its hands on its stomach; and put the remedy on a cloth evenly, and look at the limb every hour of the day or night, that the shape of the broken member does not move, or the joints are not softened; if the wound heals by the power of medicine, and give it the food we have put before, in such a way that the food is at the first subtle; and when it begins to recover, let it be large.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the shoulder and leg should be reset in 40 hours after the injury, and then one should apply heat and medicines of ointments to heal the limb.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	If the structure is crooked and swollen, it may take 1 or 2 months to reset.
de la brisure du bras	of the broken arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, called the "humerus" and "radius", where one is small and supports the elbow; and the other is large, and is the one that moves towards the little bone. Sometimes the large humerus breaks alone, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When small bones are broken, the restoration is light, and the healing; and when large bones are broken, the healing is difficult, and more painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bones that are broken, then if necessary, they should be slightly extended and aligned.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bones, then they should be stretched more forcefully; and extend them over the cushion, and tuck the thumb of the hand higher than the other fingers, and the small fingers lower than the others, and let the hairs cross over themselves, and the cushion in front of him higher than the hairs; then stretch the assistants' arms to the part outside of his hand, or to the elbow, and other assistants to the other above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then place the bones evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, put each in its place, and if there is no bone to hold it together, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make a new one as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the broken piece there is a wound, I have spoken of it to the chapter master; take care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, then use the cloth of cerate made of red oil and white wax, which is not too hard or too soft; and tie the cloth subtly, until the abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then remove the splint, and apply the plaster of flour from the mill with abundance of urine, then place the splints, and set the one of the broken bone slightly outside, and a bit wider than the others; and make sure it has six splints or more: whether the broken bone is in one of the bones, or in two; and keep it slightly above the broken bone, and always less distant, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the cloths that are on the broken bone be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, with which it is tied, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	Reward the limb and the joint after some time.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any evil accident comes to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, then you must raise the limb in hot water, until the itching is soothed; and let the limb rest without being tightly bound.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	Then continue the strapping, and if the joint is destroyed and the bones are exposed, or similar things, then apply it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling cannot come to the limb because it is too tight, then you must soften it a little, and let it rest for some time, until the swelling has gone, and then strap it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to harm, it will not last for more than 20 years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And then, they can put their hands to his neck, and make his neck even, and be careful of movement and stretching, and sleep on his back; and if this broken part is restored in 30 or 35 years, or possibly in 20 years, depending on the constitutions and compositions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breakage of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	And if it is broken in the back of the hand and we have little to do with breaks, then there will only be many tears.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the bone of the hand is broken or crushed, it is necessary that the hairs be cut straight and evenly; then place the hand on the extended board, and extend the ministers' broken bones, and put them back in their places until they are well-jointed; and apply the plaster and bandages, if there are no wounds, then place a splint according to the size of the limb; and it should be wrapped in a linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the broken bone is in the middle of the palm, make a ball of cloth, and instruct the patient to press it against his broken palm; then wrap it with a long bandage, and place the splint as big as the palm of the hand, and strap it on, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is on the other side, it is necessary to place one splint above and another below in the palm, so that the hand is open and straight, then tie it all around the hand, and bandage the joint between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture comes to one of the two, whether it is the thumb, then make it even as it should be; and strain with the palm, and if you see that you can put a straight small splint to lift the fractured bone and it does not move; and if the fracture is on the other side, as in the index or one of the others, then make it even and bind with the sound finger that is next; or you bind all together while holding them, which is better, or you put a splint above, as I have said; and pay attention to restoration and disposition of abscess, and take care of what comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken ribs
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The ribs of the ribcage are often broken, and well one sees when they return in front and behind; and the restoration is such that one lies on the side of the broken rib, and the other outside.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the hairs grow on their face, then each minister extends his bandage to his equal part; and it is when the broken rib is inserted into the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the broken rib is close to the root of the ribcage, then one bandage is placed on top of the other on the side of the broken rib, and the other bandages outside the broken rib.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the groin, and then the limbs are above the groin, and the extension below; then place the bones evenly in both hands, as according to its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the bandage, and if there are no abscesses.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there are abscesses, let it be calmed then return to your work and care; the bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap it above the fractured bone in two or three layers, and let the excess remain, then turn the leg until the toes reach the root of the foot, and tie a long thread between the calf and the leg, outside the groin, and bring the end of the thread up; then turn back over the leg and over the calf, tie the bandage, and place one bandage on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and the calf with soft cloth to equalize the compression, then begin to bandage three or four times above the fracture; and as you go higher than the fracture, and less compress; then untie the two threads that you have tied between the leg and the calf, and the three bands that are above, then return to the top of the thread, until you reach below the knee; and if it does not move from its place, then leave it like that, then there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is, then dislocate it, and address what comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that can be felt, it should be removed if possible; and if not, then the limb should be cut and pulled apart; and the cure is as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never break the ribs in such a way that one would put these stitches, as in the dislocation and arm; however, in such restoration, it does not hurt the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And it is cleaned when the ribs are restored at various times, sooner or later, according to the different constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the passage of the genuine oil
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the passage of the genuine oil, there is little breakage, but it often causes pain.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a small cut or puncture, and it heals all wounds, whether large or small, and it feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is done by applying equal pressure to the wound until it is closed as much as possible; then apply the ointment, and if you have skill, place a round bandage, and hold it as it should be, then warm all the preparations that we have said in other broken places, such as abscesses and similar things; apply to each accident what is appropriate until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the broken leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is called "mustelz" on the right side, and the other is called "foscile"; and all the fractures come as they do in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is also like that of the balanced arm, and the work is all there. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg returns to all its parts.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the "mustelz" bone is broken, it returns in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, it causes great pain and can be seen well; and it returns outwards.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore apply traction, and make it even, and tie the bandages equally; but always, it is necessary to check if the fracture is straight and well-aligned, and there are often many pieces, so that the traction is less and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two strips of cloth that gently press on the leg from one side and the other, and are as long as the leg from the knee to the groin; then wrap them around the leg above and below, and tie them in the middle as well, and at this point the leg will not decline to the right or left, and thus it is good; and no one should administer the long strip of cloth, and if it is, and properly placed on the fracture where the wound is, and move the leg every day to see if there is an abscess or other accident; so the cure until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, there is no fracture, but the bones of the foot never have a fracture and are strong, and they have only been injured in several positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture of the bones of the foot, and you see these bones protruding over each other, if you put your foot on the ground, as if it wanted to walk, then place your foot on theirs, where the bones are raised, then press them so that they return to their place; then apply the plaster and bandage above, and put a small cloth on the belly of the foot, then strap the foot evenly, then wrap bandages around it, and other things that you know how to do.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the joint is released, you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if you restore them as we have said about the two bones of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the bone, and it should be slightly wider, then put the bandage as I have described, and strain evenly; and if there are two or three or more broken, place a splint according to their quantity, wrapped in a piece of linen, and strain the bandage away from the flesh of the bone, so that it does not stick.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other breaking injuries, as soon as we have said; and treat each accident according to how it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the finger bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of the woman are broken, if the pain increases, then incline it to the part of the back, and hold it behind; then fill the wound with nature's cotton, and put in as much as possible; then lift the woman, and gently raise the back, and gradually pull out the cotton until it reaches the entrance of the nature, and the bone returns with the cotton; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has finished, return it, and do this for seven days or around: then the fracture will be restored, and if you see, take a bladder of wool, and tie a catheter to the end, and blow all the wool into the nature; then blow into the catheter until the wool is fully inflated inside: nature will return the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it in this way for some time, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the tooth of the little finger of the hand is broken, or of the woman, if it is reset as we have said in the bone of the shoulder; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and his use to this book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the fracture means in many positions the right way of restoration: understand therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the wing, when it is broken, take a goose feather and blow the wing; then wrap bandages around it, and leave it for three days or until it heals inside, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has fracture with wound, even if it is large, such as the bones of the ribs or shoulder or similar, that they be cleaned immediately, so that the cleanings that we have said bear witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is clean, and if the remaining vitriol, then begin to restore the fractured bone in the same hour, or the next day, if there are no complications.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if complications arise, then leave the restoration until the next day, until the complications are soothed, and do not touch it on the following day or quarter, for you will bring about bad accidents.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the broken jaw appears above the curve of the cheek, then it is necessary to gently place it in your hands and extend it slightly.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not even enough to be placed in your hands, then use this iron instrument, which is seven or eight spans long, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this reason, it should be three or four spans wide, according to the amount of work needed for each treatment of a broken bone; and it should be round and a bit thick, so that it does not slip when pressing against the limb at your work, and it should be pointed in front and thick in the middle, like this:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called "palainche", because the patient's arm should be placed on top of the head of the bone; and the bone is struck once, as much as it returns, and they are evenly aligned against each other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is slight, and the instruments cannot well grasp the bone, then it is necessary to cut off the head of the bone until the instruments have the ability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then with a suitable instrument, such as a saw or chisel, to your power; then cut off what remains in the bone of hardness and small scratches.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is returned, and the pain is great afterwards, wait until it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is in its natural place, then moisten the bandage with black stiff wine, and properly if it has been injured; and do not put anything oily on the wound or above it, that there be no pus and corruption; then administer these things as soon as you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and cover the bandage all around, according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not pressed with the break; many times this has been done by the foolish one, and has caused pus or death or corruption at any time; and let the strain be less and softer than other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that no evil accident has occurred, as we have said, and you relieve pain to the limb, then do not need to put above it; but wrap around, in place of above, hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two hours that the wound is bleeding again, remove what you had put above it, and apply a healing ointment to the wound, such as Tetrapharmacum and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you move the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, as long as it is sound and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs be arranged in such a way that the bow can move freely.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they continue to move too much, and it cannot be fixed but remains broken bow, cut off the small pieces of bone, because it is necessary that you wash the wound with tent, and remove all these unwanted pieces that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to the limb, or another way of corruption, then you must treat it as described in his chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the bone is broken, and open on the limb, like the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar large limbs, do not remove it immediately, because many times they die, but leave it until it can heal; perhaps it will fall off after 20 days or 30, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of the sudden blows that come to the soldering
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the healing of the breaker, precisely when it is near the joint, and the ugly thing to see is the shape of the limb; and by chance it cannot do its natural work.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Therefore take care then if it is fresh: if you administer stanching medicines, such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocollis, acacia, and similar things, in such a way that you take any of these or all together, and make them with stanching wine or with abundant honey or with garlic; and place them on the mouth of the wound, and hold it firmly, and do not let it go in your hands for a long time; and then dislodge it, and start another, until the swelling is removed; or you hold a piece of plaster well made; because the property of the plaster is that it removes all the inflammation from the limbs; and if the swelling is already hard like stone, and it is necessary to remove it, if the copper above, and making the superfluity apparent; or you reset it with any razor, until it is removed, and care for it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	a weak limb that is after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is restored, and remains after the limbs are weak and subtle, it happens for many reasons: one is because it was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many bandages, and could not come to the movements of the limb; or because of too much swelling; or because of too great movements, not in its hour; or because it has little blood in its body, then it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the pain less, and make the body tense, until the swelling is not multiplied in it; and administer baths, and give joy and rest; then put poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to the great movement, and the swelling often of high temperature, as long as the movement goes to the limb; and returns to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	a crooked limb after healing
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, however, it does not matter its natural appearance: if one believes the folk who say that one should break the limb completely, and many have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm comes, and perhaps death; however, if the dislocations and twists are fresh, then it is necessary to apply hot water or softening herbs, such as willow bark, roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the mollifying plaster, such as well-made diaquilon, and you take the willow bark powder, and mix it with goose fat or sunflower oil, and make a plaster on; or you take figs, and grind them with linseed, and similar medicines that soothe the pain.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the dislocation caused by continuously and excessively rubbing with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And allow movement to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is awake and hard, like stone, and it needs to be removed with a knife, if it covers the bone, with a slight delicate incision; and put on a poultice and bandage in the care.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, it must now be returned to its proper place.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, the joint swells, and if it is reset, it may be put back in the wrong place; for it does not matter that it is moved to its correct position: many times it brings on spasms and other pains; however, when this happens, first soothe the injury, then leave it until the abscess is relieved; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then gently reset it, and care for each member as it comes back to its proper place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the chapters on the dislocations of the shoulder joint from head to foot.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are two ways in which the mandibles can be dislocated: either they are slightly displaced from their place and somewhat softened; or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the ground, preventing the mouth from being closed and covering the tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it often returns to its proper position in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is completely and accomplished, then you must reset it quickly and not gently; and in this way, the minister should hold the head of the painful part with one hand at the root of the dislocation of the mandible within the mouth, if the dislocation is on both sides; and the other hand should be outside to make it even; and command the patient to soften his jaws and move them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And when the dislocation returns to its place evenly.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is difficult to reset, especially when both mandibles are together, then apply hot and oil, as we have said, until it is lightly reset; do not delay in resetting, as we have mentioned.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are reset evenly, and the jaw pain is relieved by softening, then apply a cloth moistened with a hot rose oil and wax mixture; then bind it lightly with soft bandages; let the patient sleep on their back, with their heads between two pillows, so they do not move to the left or right, nor try to move much, but eat light food, until the pain is gone, and the jaws are healed; then change what they want to eat lightly, and do not force them to open their mouth to chew and drink, until the jaw is fully healed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the two mandibles cannot be reset to their proper position within an hour and are not converted back to their usual place, then it may lead to fevers and swelling, and possibly diarrhea, and possibly vomiting of bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then it is a sign of danger; and many times those who have had it die within fourteen days.
de la forcelle	of the shoulder
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The shoulder cannot be dislocated from the side of its own continuity and the other, and it is not reset once dislocated, and one can feel it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient should lie on their back with their arms extended; then press the joint gently into your palm, and it will return; then apply the plaster and bandage, and hold it in place; if the one who is facing the side cannot be dislocated, then if they are not, and if they are dislocated once, then reset the joint as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and hold it in place, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and thus the same is done with the shoulder, when it is free from its joint.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated: one is that it is dislocated at the part of the acromion above; and the second is at the part of the pis; and sometimes dislocated at the part above, and this happens rarely; and does not dislocate behind for the shoulder, and does not dislocate inside for the nerves; and many times dislocated upwards towards the acromion, especially to those who have little fat, because to these it is painful; to those who have enough fat, it is painful, and returns painfully.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, some men have a blow or a crushing, and the shoulder swells with an abscess, and they think it is dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Then you must examine it, until you are certain; and then the treatment begins.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that the dislocation is when it is below the acromion, and it sets apart the sick shoulder from the healthy one, and you will find between them a difference; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and below the acromion the top of the shoulder, like as if it were one bone; and it cannot move its hand to its neck, nor any movements; and thus, if it is dislocated above, it is not hidden, for you will see it clearly below; and this way of dislocation is not hidden, when it is new, or if the pain is in the top.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The method is that the assistant lifts the injured arm upwards, then places their fingers below the joint, and forces the joint back into place from above; the assistant lifts the arm and extends it upwards, then removes it quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if she does not come as we have said afterwards, then it is necessary to bathe the injured arm in hot water; and the assistant should rub and soothe it with a decoction of althea and fenugreek and melilot in hot water, and apply it; then place the injured arm on its back, and place a cloth evenly, neither too soft nor too hard, under the joint, then place the foot of the shoulder on the cloth, and gently lift the shoulder and draw the hand away from the injured arm; another assistant should wash the head of the shoulder so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder is now completely healed, and if you see that the dislocation returns according to this method: then you must find someone who is stronger than the injured arm; and stand on the side of the body, and push the shoulder away from the joint, and lift the joint upwards, so that the injured arm hangs down; and another assistant should draw the hand of the injured arm down towards the stomach.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the pain is too light, you can move it with anything heavy, and the dislocation now returns.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And the resetting can also be done in another way: and it is that you place a long, thin piece of wood in the ground, which the patient should hold as if it were a staff, and not too thick or too sharp; then it should be placed outside the dislocated joint, but with cloth underneath, and the joint should be stretched out as far as possible on the other side, and the joint will return to its place quickly; and if it does not return for all these things we have said, then do this cure: take a piece of wood that is two arms wide and four fingers thick, which has a point that enters from the front outside the shoulder, in this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie above the shoulder with soft cloths, which was not too tight to cause pain, then remove it from under the dislocation; and extend one arm over the long one, and tie the help sus the long one, and the arm at the head of the hand, then put the arm over the wide end of an arrow, and hold the hands down, and let the body hang from the other side: the joint is now healed.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is healed in any way, it is necessary to place a soft cloth under the dislocation, then apply the plaster mixed with flour from the mill, with incense and a little egg, over the whole shoulder and around, then remove the plaster from under the dislocation evenly, and turn the limb back onto the plaster, and embrace the hand to its neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he change it little, until the limb is comfortable, for it will heal faster; and then change it after five or seven days, and move it; and if it is stiff and not softened, then it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is very strong due to moisture that has come, or for another reason, it is necessary that you administer cautery at three points, as it is placed in front or in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot lift the arm up, then cut or stretch or soften the nerve at the head of the shoulder; and cut that the joint has never been healed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is by the ankle and the knees, or behind, is made by pushing and stretching of hands, and there is another remedy; and treat until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the member becomes swollen and still moves, then use the remedy many times, until that swelling is alleviated, and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	That the joint of the shoulder is dislocated at points, and repeatedly dislocates; and it has been dislocated from all parts, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, for one can see and feel it well; and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with the healthy one, make sure to see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is broken, and cannot move the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it as soon as possible when the shoulder blade comes, for if the shoulder blade comes, it would be painful to reset; and perhaps it cannot be reset entirely at all, especially when it is in the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more great pain, and perhaps it kills the patient.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it is such that one can reset it, that you extend your hand to their two hands; and their arms are spread out, and their hands on either side of the shoulder, outside and inside, and push the joint back together, or at the root of their palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, then it returns when he doubles his hand to his hand, and trusts the root of the palm which is misaligned.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if he does not want to return to its place, then apply strong extension; and it is that two ministers extend the arm, and they hold the arm with two ministers, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from both sides, then when you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint at the joint, if there is any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, until it returns; and when it is in its place, then put a dry plaster with some honey on top, and press it together, and can the arm against the back of the bad shoulder, and leave it for some time, then remove it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firm in its place, then release the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not hold well, then restart the bandage and the limb, and leave it thus for some time, until it is firmly put back; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and rub him well, and press until it is soothed; or place a piece of fat lamb grease on the joint, leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and put him in a bath; when he urinates, rub the joint immediately, then place the grease back, and put him in a bath again; do this twice or three times until he is healed; and if you see, then place a piece of moist, warm chaff with butter on it, and strain it; it will return to its normal position.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The joint of the hand is dislocated, and the return is lighter than other joints. Therefore, it should be quickly returned to its place as soon as it is dislocated, whether the skin is swollen or there is an abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And the return is that you place the misaligned hand on a table, and extend the fingers of the hand, and place the palm so that it aligns with the appearance of the joint, and press it until it returns fully. Then, you should check if it is properly aligned; therefore, place the misaligned side of the hand on a table for extension and return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, put the hairs on the back of your hand over the table, and the eyes put their hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, it is well; if not, apply the soothing plasters and let it rest until you can try again.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if it cannot be borne, and you cannot put it back in place after some time, the joint will remain twisted; and do not try to straighten anything until the hand is wet, and nothing can be stretched at all: then cut the nerves or the artery; otherwise, there is no other means than to stretch by fire through the skin, and perhaps it is not worth it.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, put the plaster that we have mentioned above, then strap it and leave it for 3 days, then remove it and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it cannot move well, and there is no swelling, then apply hot wool, and rub until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Fingers are not dislocated at any part of the hand, never at the back of the palm or on the wrist; then place the two fingers, and maintain the dislocation with your fists until it returns, then support the head of the finger, and move it towards the part where it is disjointed; and leave it for 2 days, and then put it in place; and tie it as we have said, and remove the bandage the next day, and move it, and reattach it; and do this often, until it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated on the wrist of the hand, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same when it is dislocated in other parts.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the spine from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine of the back or neck is dislocated, and there are many dislocations, there is no cure, for the patient dies from the pain.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excretions jump suddenly without volition, and they cannot hold it, and often all the limbs are softened, or the two legs or the two arms or one; and often the spine moves to the fourth part; that which moves to the back is called "gillbositez": the cure is that you reward the gillbositez if it comes from childhood: if there is no cure or healing for the whole.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And those that come from falling or from similar things, they used the old methods of treatment with great words, but I have abbreviated them according to my intention and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the case of a fracture that comes from the front, there is no engineering or healing; and so with the one that comes directly to the second rib, and one cannot cure it other than by the proper one that comes to the back, as I said; and it is that the wounds should be extended over its face in one place evenly, and have some strain away from him, that he does not swell; then make one bandage at the head in earth form, and the other at the feet, and tie a ligature outside the fracture, and the other as hips, and as shoulders, and as knees; and the assistant should bind the ligatures, the ones at the head and the others at the feet, among the two bandages; and they should be well fastened, the bandage as we have said, and the fingers put its palms over the spine properly, until it returns.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return by this cure, take a long board of three arms in length, and twist it out of shape, and place the hairs on one side, and put the head of the board from one side, then place the middle of the board on the spine; and put the mirrors his feet on the other end of the board, and press well, until it returns to its place; and if you see, do the same with the other side.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should tie two ropes to the head of the shoulder of one arm, and on both sides of the feet, and between each rope, outside and inside, a long palm; and in each rope, a small hole, where the turner goes, and so that the ropes are firmly on the ground, so that they do not move; and between each two ropes, there is one turning rope, along with the other turners, and two small ropes of a long palm to turn the turner; and then tie the ligament that is among the tendons to the turner's head, and the other ligament to the other turner's feet, and each minister turns his turner along the entire ligament, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, apply a desiccating plaster with abundant sulfur, and then pour in, and then place the end of a tablet of three fingers long, which holds the neck of the vertebrae and the part of the spine healthy, then tie it with a bandage as we have said, and use subtle pressure until they are healed; and if something comes at the end of health, then administer medicines that are softening and astringent, with the remedy that we have mentioned before; and never give one piece of plaster, and never come to appear in the back spine of the back, and pay attention that this is dislocation; and it is the bone that opens, because one should not have presumption: perhaps it would cause death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of shoulder dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	It is said that the joints of the shoulder and the joints of the back do not come out except for dislocations only, and they do not come out as with other joints; and the joint of the back is dislocated in four parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside then, and slightly dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of this dislocation inside is such that when one joins the crooked leg with the straight one, it is longer and more open than the healthy ones, and cannot bend its knee to the fire; and the legs that are swollen with abscesses are those that are located below, because the cause of the belly comes from there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of one who comes after this is that this accident is opposite to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of one who has come before are that he stands well on his leg according to completion; however, he does not double over with pain in the groin, and if one wants to make him walk, he cannot do so, and retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of one who has come after are that he cannot spread his groin, nor bend, and his leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated to the side of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The treatment of this kind of dislocation is that you wait for the dislocation to heal, and it stays according to its condition, if there is no cure; and there is no need for him to have presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in this kind of dislocation where the dislocation is fresh, and there are four ways of dislocation, you must quickly return the joint, and extend and bend it, and move it to the left and right; perhaps if it returns, and there is no need for other treatment.
