Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must apply one strong minister, and bend the leg strongly at two joints, or one that is tied above the knee; and other ministers extend their hand above in a similar manner as they push their hands out of their sockets, then pinch the skin of the back; and some grip the head of the limb; and stretch up and down all at once, until the pain is lifted from the ground at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common for four similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned as we have said, then it is well.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must treat its similar case. When the dislocation is at the pectoral, then you should support the misaligned part on its healthy side, then place the ligament at the base of the ribcage, and the limb that is outside the arm, then extend the ligament above the arm, and towards the shoulder; then take other ministers to grasp the large rib of the misaligned ribcage, and extend it back into its place: if it returns to its limb now; and this method of dislocation is less severe than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this manner that we have said, then it is necessary to tie the two hairs of the injured leg together with a strong rope above the two heels, and above the two knees, and let the injured leg be stretched out two fingers more than the other; then hang it suspended by the chief of a stick, and let the other arm be suspended from the ground; then command the minister to grasp the base of the neck, and let another minister hang with the injured leg, who grasps the neck properly, for the joint is now approaching.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is on the other side, then grasp the injured leg, as we have said in the case of gout, and hold the rope properly above the injured leg and also at the feet; then put two bands, one at the head and the other at the foot, then fold the band between the thighs of the injured leg in the proper form; and wrap moist cloths around it, so that it does not become stiff, then extend each minister towards him, and the master places the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, place it on the table, and press it as we have said in the gilbosite, and cut off the hairs on the clean side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the injured leg quickly, and as I have said; and place the fingers of your pain on the other side of the injured limb, then press with the other hand, and extend it down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is in the back, it is not necessary to extend the injured leg downwards, nor to lift it up, but it should be as it was when it was dislocated in the back, as we have said for the lying-in of both hips; and it should be on its face, and the limb extended as we have said before, and one must press on the joint at the table; and it will be perfect when the injured leg extends its legs, and they are even; then support the knees, and put the poultice, and the bandage of a bundle, so that the hip does not move; and let it rest for three or four days, then remove it, and put the poultice on; and if you see that they are even, then the bandage, as before, and let it rest for three days; then remove it, and make the limb strong again, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the shoulder dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulder is dislocated in three ways: that is to say, from the inside and outside, and behind; and it does not dislocate from the front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his leg at the knee, and if he cannot straighten it at the knee, then it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back against his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his shoulder to your palms, and bring it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the shoulder correctly; and another minister extends his foot, until the shoulder returns to its place, and the signs are that he holds his leg at the knee lightly; and put the plaster on it, and make the leg and knee rub together strongly for three or four hours, then release it; and do not work on the patient again until the limb is comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	If the limbs are not properly aligned, administer strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the back, until they are healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the ankle.
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The feet are never splinted and never fully dislocated, neither inside nor outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the bone is displaced, and it feels tender to the touch at the part where it is dislocated: the swelling is slight, and one should gently extend it slightly when it is splinted only.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated completely, one should first straighten the bone correctly, and hold it firmly with one's hands on the leg, above the knee; then pull the tendon to you with your right hand, and then with your left hand twice, then extend it upwards, and gently tap the tendon above; do this twice as we have said, both bending and pulling the tendon; if it returns, it is good; if not, repeat the procedure, for it will return; and if it cannot return in this way, place the dislocated bone on its back on the ground, and firmly fix the tendon between its thighs, so that it does not bend the bone; then bandage the tendon with a cloth, and other ministers extend the tendon to your hands or to the injured limb, so that they can hold the tendon while stretching; then extend all the ministers equally, and the tendons should be held between the thighs of the dislocated bone to keep it in place while stretching; then put the mires evenly on the dislocation at your hands, and other ministers bandage the leg cleanly outside, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when she goes to the point, put the plaster and make it wet above, and the stain forms, and tie the leg to the thigh, and keep the nerves that are above the knee behind, so that the joints are not too tight; then leave her for two or three days, and if the joints break, remove the plaster; then let her go on the third day or fourth, and defend against the pain for four days; and if she goes before that time, it is not sure that she will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, it is necessary that you calm it down, as we have said elsewhere, until it is healed.
des dois	For the fire cautery, instruct
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the shoulder is dislocated, if it is properly extended and moved, it is a simple matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is not in any way towards the back or the front, then you should make the patient sit with their arm extended straight out or on a table, and place your hand over the joint, then press firmly until it realigns; and when it is aligned and there is no opening, place a board under the elbow at the same angle as the shoulder, then press firmly for three days, then release; and let it rest until it is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and of dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, often the pain is great: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, and do not know the art well, and have not used it for a long time, and are not merciful and slow, and not harsh; at the beginning of things, gently treat abscesses, and leave the pain in God’s hands, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then now reset the member to its place, as long as the abscesses are gone; and when the member is in place, then administer things to heal abscesses, and cure the wound, as it should be, with frequent dressings; and if with dislocation there is a fracture, and small bones are broken, then remove them, and do what we have said in simple diseases; and guard against entering the path of fear, as I have said, for it is better for you according to your Creator, and for the knowledge of your armor and body.
